L. System Design — DevOps Perspective

Senior Level

High Availability Design Principles

  • Eliminate single points of failure: Every component should have at least 2 instances
  • Multi-AZ deployments: Distribute across Availability Zones within a region
  • Health checks everywhere: LB, K8s probes, application-level
  • Circuit breakers: Stop cascading failures (Hystrix, Resilience4j)
  • Timeouts and retries: Every external call must have a timeout + bounded retry
  • Graceful degradation: Serve cached content when database is down

Zero Downtime Deployment Strategies

StrategyHowRollbackCostRisk
Rolling UpdateReplace pods one by oneAutomatic via K8sLowBrief mixed versions
Blue-GreenFull parallel env, switch trafficInstant (switch back)2x infra costLow
CanaryRoute 5% → new, ramp upRoute back to oldSlight increaseVery low
A/B TestingSplit by user segmentChange routing ruleModerateLow
RecreateStop all, start newNone (downtime)NoneHigh (downtime)
BLUE-GREEN DEPLOYMENT: Before: After: ┌─────────┐ 100% traffic ┌─────────┐ 0% traffic │ BLUE │<────────────── │ BLUE │ │ v1.0 │ (active) │ v1.0 │ (idle) └─────────┘ └─────────┘ ┌─────────┐ 0% traffic ┌─────────┐ 100% traffic │ GREEN │ │ GREEN │<────────────── │ v2.0 │ (idle) │ v2.0 │ (active) └─────────┘ └─────────┘ CANARY DEPLOYMENT: v1.0 (old) ←── 95% traffic v2.0 (new) ←── 5% traffic After testing → 50/50 → 100% to v2.0

Interview Questions — System Design

Design a deployment pipeline for a high-traffic e-commerce site (10M users).
1) Source: GitHub + branch protection (required reviewers, passing tests). 2) CI: GitHub Actions — lint, unit, integration tests in parallel. Security scan (Trivy, Snyk). 3) Artifact: Docker image pushed to ECR, tagged with git SHA. 4) Staging: Auto-deploy to staging EKS. Run smoke + load tests. 5) Production: Manual approval gate. Canary deploy 5% → 20% → 100% with automated rollback on error rate spike. 6) Monitoring: Prometheus alerts, Grafana dashboards, PagerDuty for on-call. 7) Rollback: kubectl rollout undo in <2 minutes.
How do you achieve database zero-downtime migrations in CI/CD?
Use expand-contract (parallel change) pattern: 1) Expand: Deploy migration that adds new column as nullable (backward compatible). Run alongside old code. 2) Migrate: Backfill existing rows. 3) Contract: Deploy new application code that uses new column. 4) Cleanup: Remove old column in a later migration. Never: rename columns in one step, add NOT NULL without default, drop columns while old code still runs. Use tools like Flyway or Liquibase with versioned migrations in the repo.
🎯

Interview Master Section

All Levels

Beginner Questions (0–1 year)

What is DevOps and why is it important?
DevOps is a culture and set of practices that combines software development (Dev) and IT operations (Ops) to shorten the development lifecycle and deliver high quality software continuously. It breaks down the traditional wall between developers (write code) and operations (run infrastructure). Key benefits: faster releases (from months to hours), more reliable systems, quicker recovery from failures, and better collaboration. Companies like Netflix, Amazon, and Google release code thousands of times per day using DevOps principles.
What is the difference between Docker and a Virtual Machine?
VMs virtualize hardware — each VM has a full OS (GBs of overhead), managed by a hypervisor. Boot time: minutes. Containers share the host OS kernel — only the app and its dependencies are packaged. Size: MBs. Boot time: milliseconds. Containers are more lightweight and faster, but less isolated (share kernel). VMs offer stronger isolation. In practice, containers run inside VMs in production (EC2 running Docker or K8s).
Explain what version control is and why it matters.
Version control (Git) tracks every change to code — who made it, when, and why. Benefits: 1) History — revert to any previous version. 2) Collaboration — multiple developers work simultaneously without overwriting each other. 3) Branching — experiment safely without affecting main codebase. 4) Audit trail — required for compliance in many industries. Without it, teams email zip files of code, accidentally overwrite each other's work, and can't recover from bugs.
What is SSH and how does key-based authentication work?
SSH (Secure Shell) is an encrypted protocol for remote server access. Key-based auth uses asymmetric cryptography: you have a private key (never leave your machine) and a public key (placed on server in ~/.ssh/authorized_keys). When connecting, the server sends a challenge encrypted with your public key — only your private key can decrypt it, proving your identity without sending a password over the network. More secure than passwords: no brute-force risk, no phishing. Generate with: ssh-keygen -t ed25519 -C "email@example.com".

Intermediate Questions (2–4 years)

How would you implement zero-downtime deployments?
Multiple approaches: 1) Rolling update (K8s default): replace pods one at a time, keep minAvailable=1. 2) Blue-Green: run two identical environments, switch load balancer. Instant rollback by switching back. 3) Canary: route 5% traffic to new version, monitor error rates, gradually increase. 4) Feature flags: deploy code with feature disabled, enable for users gradually. Key requirements for all: health checks, graceful shutdown (SIGTERM handling, drain connections), session affinity or stateless design, database migration backward compatibility.
Explain Kubernetes networking — how does a request reach a Pod?
Request flow: 1) Client → LoadBalancer (cloud LB, e.g. ELB) 2) → Ingress Controller (nginx-ingress pod) based on host/path rules 3) → Service (ClusterIP) via iptables/IPVS rules managed by kube-proxy 4) → Pod (selected by service's label selector). Key: every Pod gets a unique cluster-IP. Services provide stable DNS names and load-balance across pods. kube-proxy on each node programs iptables rules that intercept service traffic and forward to pod IPs. Overlay networks (Calico, Flannel) enable cross-node pod communication.
What is Terraform state and why must it be stored remotely?
Terraform state is a JSON file (.tfstate) that maps your HCL resources to real cloud resources. Terraform reads state to know what exists before computing a plan. Remote storage (S3 + DynamoDB) is critical for teams because: 1) Shared source of truth — all team members and CI/CD see the same state. 2) State locking (DynamoDB) — prevents two concurrent applies from corrupting state. 3) Backup — S3 versioning lets you recover from corrupted state. 4) Encryption — state contains sensitive values (passwords, keys). Local state in git = accidental secret exposure + merge conflicts.
How do you monitor a microservices application?
Three pillars: 1) Metrics (Prometheus): RED method — Rate (requests/sec), Errors (error rate), Duration (latency p50/p99) per service. Alert on SLO violations. 2) Logs (ELK/Loki): Structured JSON logs with correlation IDs. Centralize all logs. Alert on error patterns. 3) Traces (Jaeger/Zipkin): Distributed tracing — follow a request across 10+ microservices. Find where latency comes from. Also: synthetic monitoring (uptime checks), dashboards in Grafana, on-call rotation with PagerDuty. Use SLOs (Service Level Objectives) to define acceptable reliability.

Advanced / Senior Questions (5+ years)

Your team is deploying 50+ times per day. How do you maintain stability?
1) Automated testing at every layer — unit (fast), integration, e2e, contract tests. 2) Progressive delivery: every deploy starts as canary (1% → 10% → 100%). 3) Automated rollback: if error rate spikes >1% or latency doubles during deploy, automated system rolls back. 4) Feature flags: decouple deploy from release — code ships dark, feature enabled independently. 5) Observability: real-time dashboards showing golden signals during every deploy. 6) Immutable infrastructure: each deploy creates new instances, never modify in place. 7) Database migrations backward-compatible always. 8) Chaos engineering: intentional failure injection to validate resilience.
How would you design a multi-region disaster recovery strategy?
Depends on RTO/RPO requirements: 1) Active-Passive (Pilot Light): minimal infrastructure in DR region, scale up on disaster. RPO: hours. RTO: hours. Cheapest. 2) Warm Standby: reduced-scale running environment in DR, scale up fast. RPO: minutes. RTO: minutes. 3) Active-Active: traffic served from both regions simultaneously. RPO: near-zero. RTO: seconds. Most expensive. Key components: Route 53 health checks + latency routing, data replication (RDS Read Replica promote, DynamoDB Global Tables, S3 Cross-Region Replication), regular DR drills (monthly failover tests), runbooks for each failure scenario.
How do you handle secrets rotation without downtime?
1) Use dynamic secrets (HashiCorp Vault): application requests credential with TTL, Vault creates/rotates automatically. 2) Dual-credential rotation: step 1 create new credential, step 2 update app to accept both, step 3 rotate all apps to new credential, step 4 revoke old. 3) External Secrets Operator in K8s: Vault/AWS Secrets Manager → K8s Secret, triggers pod rolling restart on change. 4) Application must handle credential refresh without restart (connection pool reconnect). 5) Never hard-code secrets in images, env vars in plain text, or config files checked into git.

Scenario-Based Questions

Real-World Scenario

Production database is at 95% disk capacity. You have 1 hour before it fills up.

Immediate (0-10 min): Alert team, check what's consuming space: du -sh /var/lib/mysql/*. Check for binary logs: SHOW BINARY LOGS; If safe: PURGE BINARY LOGS BEFORE NOW() - INTERVAL 3 DAY;

Short-term (10-30 min): Delete old log files if not needed. Clear temp tables. Move old partitions to archive storage.

Medium-term (30-60 min): Add disk volume (AWS: modify EBS volume, expand filesystem online). Trigger manual backup and archive old data.

Post-incident: Set CloudWatch alarm at 75% disk. Implement automated log rotation. Schedule regular archival jobs. Review data retention policy.

Real-World Scenario

After a deploy, 502 errors spike to 30%. Rollback or fix-forward?

Decision criteria: Time to fix vs time to rollback.

1) Check new pod logs: kubectl logs -l app=myapp --since=5m. Common causes: missing env var, wrong port, failed DB connection.

2) If root cause clear and fix is <5 lines: fix forward — patch, push, pipeline deploys in 3 min.

3) If root cause unclear: rollback immediately: kubectl rollout undo deployment/myapp. Then investigate with full logs.

4) Communicate: Slack/status page update within 5 minutes of detection.

5) Post-mortem within 48 hours: timeline, root cause, action items.

HR & Behavioral Questions

Tell me about a production incident you handled. How did you resolve it?
Use STAR format — Situation, Task, Action, Result. Example structure: "We had a memory leak in production that was causing pods to OOMKill every 4-6 hours, impacting 15% of users. My task was to find and fix it under pressure. I used kubectl top + Prometheus to identify the specific pod and service. I added heap profiling and identified a connection pool that wasn't being released. I deployed a fix, monitored for 2 hours with no recurrence, and added a memory alert at 75% to catch it early next time. This reduced incidents by 100% for that service and I documented it as a runbook."
How do you stay updated with DevOps tools and practices?
Good answers: Follow CNCF landscape for cloud-native tools. Read: KubeWeekly, DevOps Weekly newsletter, AWS blog, HashiCorp blog. Follow practitioners on LinkedIn/Twitter (Kelsey Hightower, Liz Fong-Jones). Attend KubeCon, AWS re:Invent talks (free on YouTube). Personal lab: home lab or free-tier AWS for experimenting. Certifications: CKA, AWS SAA, Terraform Associate. Contribute to open source or write about what you learn (blog/GitHub).
How do you handle disagreements with developers about deployment procedures?
Empathy first — understand their concern (usually speed vs safety). Bring data: show historical incident rate, mean time to recover. Collaborate on solutions that meet both needs (e.g., feature flags let developers ship fast while ops controls risk). Document procedures so it's not personal — "the policy says X, let's follow it and revisit if it's wrong." If persistent disagreement, escalate to engineering leadership with written proposal from both sides. The goal is shared: reliable, fast delivery.
🚀

Real-World Projects

Hands-On

Project 1 — Deploy Static App with Docker

Level: Beginner Time: 2-3 hours Tools: Docker, Nginx

Architecture

User → Browser → Nginx Container (port 80) → Static HTML/CSS/JS files

Steps

1
Create a simple static website: 
mkdir myapp && cd myapp
cat > index.html << 'EOF'
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html>
<head><title>My DevOps App</title></head>
<body>
  <h1>Deployed with Docker!</h1>
  <p>Version: <span id="version">1.0.0</span></p>
</body>
</html>
EOF
2
Create Dockerfile: 
cat > Dockerfile << 'EOF'
FROM nginx:alpine
COPY index.html /usr/share/nginx/html/
COPY nginx.conf /etc/nginx/nginx.conf
EXPOSE 80
CMD ["nginx", "-g", "daemon off;"]
EOF
3
Create nginx.conf: 
events { worker_connections 1024; }
http {
  server {
    listen 80;
    root /usr/share/nginx/html;
    gzip on;
    add_header X-Frame-Options "SAMEORIGIN";
    add_header X-Content-Type-Options "nosniff";
  }
}
4
Build and run: 
docker build -t myapp:1.0 .
docker run -d -p 8080:80 --name myapp myapp:1.0
# Open http://localhost:8080
5
Add .dockerignore and verify size: 
echo "*.md\n.git\nnode_modules" > .dockerignore
docker images myapp        # should be ~10MB
docker inspect myapp
Expected output: Website accessible at http://localhost:8080. Image size under 15MB using Alpine base.
Extension: Push to Docker Hub, then deploy to AWS EC2 or App Runner.

Project 2 — CI/CD Pipeline with GitHub Actions + Docker

Level: Intermediate Time: 4-6 hours Tools: GitHub Actions, Docker, EC2

Architecture

GitHub Push → GitHub Actions → Build & Test → Docker Build → ECR/DockerHub → Deploy to EC2

Full Pipeline Setup

# .github/workflows/main.yml
name: Build and Deploy

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
  pull_request:
    branches: [main]

env:
  REGISTRY: ghcr.io
  IMAGE_NAME: ${{ github.repository }}

jobs:
  test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - name: Setup Node.js
        uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with: { node-version: '20', cache: 'npm' }
      - run: npm ci
      - run: npm test

  build:
    needs: test
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    outputs:
      image-tag: ${{ steps.meta.outputs.tags }}
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Login to GHCR
        uses: docker/login-action@v3
        with:
          registry: ghcr.io
          username: ${{ github.actor }}
          password: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}

      - name: Generate tags
        id: meta
        uses: docker/metadata-action@v5
        with:
          images: ${{ env.REGISTRY }}/${{ env.IMAGE_NAME }}
          tags: |
            type=sha,prefix=sha-
            type=raw,value=latest,enable=${{ github.ref == 'refs/heads/main' }}

      - name: Build and push
        uses: docker/build-push-action@v5
        with:
          context: .
          push: ${{ github.ref == 'refs/heads/main' }}
          tags: ${{ steps.meta.outputs.tags }}
          cache-from: type=gha
          cache-to: type=gha,mode=max

  deploy:
    needs: build
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
    steps:
      - name: Deploy to EC2
        uses: appleboy/ssh-action@v1.0.3
        with:
          host: ${{ secrets.EC2_HOST }}
          username: ubuntu
          key: ${{ secrets.EC2_SSH_KEY }}
          script: |
            echo ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }} | \
              docker login ghcr.io -u ${{ github.actor }} --password-stdin
            docker pull ghcr.io/${{ github.repository }}:latest
            docker stop myapp || true
            docker rm myapp || true
            docker run -d \
              --name myapp \
              -p 80:3000 \
              --restart unless-stopped \
              -e NODE_ENV=production \
              ghcr.io/${{ github.repository }}:latest
            docker image prune -f
Expected outcome: Every push to main builds, tests, and deploys automatically within 3-5 minutes.

Project 3 — Kubernetes Deployment with Full Monitoring

Level: Advanced Time: 1-2 days Tools: K8s, Helm, Prometheus, Grafana, Terraform

Architecture

Internet │ ┌───────┴────────┐ │ Ingress-Nginx │ (Helm) └───────┬────────┘ │ ┌──────────┼──────────┐ │ │ │ ┌────┴───┐ ┌───┴────┐ ┌───┴────┐ │ App │ │ App │ │ App │ (3 replicas) │ Pod 1 │ │ Pod 2 │ │ Pod 3 │ └────┬───┘ └───┬────┘ └───┬────┘ │ │ │ ┌────┴─────────┴──────────┴────┐ │ PostgreSQL (StatefulSet)│ └───────────────────────────────┘ Monitoring Stack: Prometheus → scrapes all pods Grafana → dashboards Alertmanager → Slack alerts

Step-by-Step

1
Bootstrap cluster (use EKS or kind for local): 
# Local: kind
kind create cluster --name devops-demo --config kind-config.yaml

# AWS EKS via Terraform
module "eks" {
  source  = "terraform-aws-modules/eks/aws"
  version = "~> 20.0"
  cluster_name    = "devops-demo"
  cluster_version = "1.29"
  vpc_id          = module.vpc.vpc_id
  subnet_ids      = module.vpc.private_subnets
  eks_managed_node_groups = {
    main = {
      min_size     = 2
      max_size     = 10
      desired_size = 3
      instance_types = ["t3.medium"]
    }
  }
}
2
Install monitoring stack via Helm: 
# Add repos
helm repo add prometheus-community \
  https://prometheus-community.github.io/helm-charts
helm repo add grafana https://grafana.github.io/helm-charts
helm repo update

# Install kube-prometheus-stack (Prometheus + Grafana + Alertmanager)
helm upgrade --install monitoring \
  prometheus-community/kube-prometheus-stack \
  --namespace monitoring --create-namespace \
  --set grafana.adminPassword=securepassword \
  --set prometheus.prometheusSpec.retention=15d \
  --set alertmanager.config.receivers[0].name=slack \
  -f monitoring-values.yaml
3
Deploy app with all K8s objects: 
kubectl apply -f - << 'EOF'
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: myapp
  namespace: production
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels: {app: myapp}
  template:
    metadata:
      labels: {app: myapp}
      annotations:
        prometheus.io/scrape: "true"
        prometheus.io/port: "3000"
        prometheus.io/path: "/metrics"
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: myapp
        image: myorg/myapp:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 3000
        resources:
          requests: {memory: 128Mi, cpu: 100m}
          limits: {memory: 256Mi, cpu: 500m}
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet: {path: /health, port: 3000}
          initialDelaySeconds: 10
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet: {path: /health, port: 3000}
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: Service
metadata:
  name: myapp
  namespace: production
spec:
  selector: {app: myapp}
  ports:
  - port: 80
    targetPort: 3000
EOF
4
Install and configure Ingress: 
helm upgrade --install ingress-nginx \
  ingress-nginx/ingress-nginx \
  --namespace ingress-nginx --create-namespace \
  --set controller.metrics.enabled=true \
  --set controller.metrics.serviceMonitor.enabled=true

# Apply Ingress rule
kubectl apply -f ingress.yaml
5
Verify everything: 
kubectl get pods -n production
kubectl get pods -n monitoring
# Port-forward Grafana
kubectl port-forward -n monitoring svc/monitoring-grafana 3000:80
# Open localhost:3000, login with admin/securepassword
# Import dashboard: Kubernetes/Compute Resources/Namespace
Expected: 3-replica app running, metrics scraped by Prometheus, visible in Grafana, alerts configured for CPU/Memory/error rates.

Common Errors & Fixes

Troubleshooting
ErrorCauseFix
Permission denied (publickey)SSH key not added or wrong userssh-add ~/.ssh/id_ed25519 or check ~/.ssh/authorized_keys on server
EACCES: permission deniednpm install as root, wrong dir permissionssudo chown -R $USER ~/.npm
Docker: port already in useAnother process on that portss -tulpn | grep :8080 then kill or change port
K8s: ImagePullBackOffWrong image name, missing registry credsCheck image name, create imagePullSecret, verify registry access
K8s: OOMKilledContainer exceeded memory limitIncrease limits or fix memory leak in app
Terraform: Error acquiring the state lockPrevious apply crashed, lock stuckterraform force-unlock LOCK_ID
Terraform: Resource already existsResource created outside Terraformterraform import resource.name id
Ansible: unreachableSSH connection failedCheck host IP, SSH key, security groups
Git: rejected (non-fast-forward)Remote has commits you don't havegit pull --rebase origin main then push
Nginx: 502 Bad GatewayBackend not running or wrong portCheck backend service, verify proxy_pass URL
Docker: no space left on deviceDocker images/containers filling diskdocker system prune -af
AWS: UnauthorizedOperationIAM permissions missingCheck IAM policy, attach required permission
K8s: Pending (Insufficient memory)Nodes don't have enough resourcesAdd nodes to cluster or reduce resource requests
CORS errorBrowser blocked cross-origin requestAdd Access-Control-Allow-Origin header on API server

Certifications Roadmap

2-4 weeks prep. Validates cloud/Linux fundamentals.

2-3 months each. Core credentials most employers require.

Production Best Practices Summary

  • Never hardcode secrets — use Vault, AWS Secrets Manager, or K8s Secrets with External Secrets Operator
  • Immutable infrastructure — never SSH into prod to make changes; change comes through automation
  • Everything in version control — infra code, app code, runbooks, configs
  • Test in production-like environments — staging should mirror prod exactly
  • Automate toil — if you do it more than twice, automate it
  • Design for failure — assume any component can fail at any time
  • Practice runbooks — document AND drill failure scenarios
  • Blameless post-mortems — focus on systems, not people; share learnings
  • Shift security left — scan code, dependencies, images in CI before production
  • Resource limits always — every container must have CPU/memory limits in K8s
⚙️

Project 4 — 2-Tier Production LEMP Stack on AWS with ALB

Intermediate

Deploy a production website across two EC2 instances: one running the application (Nginx + PHP-FPM) accessible via a public ALB, and one running MySQL in a private subnet — both wired together behind an Application Load Balancer.

Architecture Overview

Internet │ ┌────────────┴────────────┐ │ Application Load Balancer│ ← public, port 80/443 │ (ALB — us-east-1) │ └────────────┬────────────┘ │ HTTP :80 ┌────────────▼────────────┐ │ VPC │ │ ┌──────────────────┐ │ │ │ Public Subnet │ │ │ │ 10.0.1.0/24 │ │ │ │ │ │ │ │ ┌────────────┐ │ │ │ │ │ App EC2 │ │ │ ← SSH allowed (port 22) │ │ │ (Nginx + │ │ │ │ │ │ PHP-FPM) │ │ │ │ │ │ Public IP │ │ │ │ │ └─────┬──────┘ │ │ │ └────────│─────────┘ │ │ │ port 3306 │ │ ┌────────▼─────────┐ │ │ │ Private Subnet │ │ │ │ 10.0.2.0/24 │ │ │ │ │ │ │ │ ┌────────────┐ │ │ │ │ │ MySQL EC2 │ │ │ ← No public IP │ │ │ (MySQL 8) │ │ │ │ │ └────────────┘ │ │ │ └──────────────────┘ │ └─────────────────────────┘
LEMP = Linux + ENginx + MySQL + PHP. This is the standard production stack for WordPress, Laravel, and custom PHP apps.

Prerequisites

  • AWS account with IAM user having EC2, VPC, ELB full access
  • AWS CLI configured: aws configure
  • An EC2 Key Pair created in your target region
  • Domain name (optional — for HTTPS via ACM)

Step 1 — Create VPC & Subnets

# Create VPC
aws ec2 create-vpc --cidr-block 10.0.0.0/16 \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=vpc,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=lemp-vpc}]'
# Note the VpcId returned, e.g. vpc-0abc123

VPC_ID=vpc-0abc123   # replace with your VpcId

# Enable DNS hostnames (required for EC2 hostname resolution)
aws ec2 modify-vpc-attribute --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --enable-dns-hostnames '{"Value":true}'
aws ec2 modify-vpc-attribute --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --enable-dns-support '{"Value":true}'

# Create Internet Gateway and attach
IGW_ID=$(aws ec2 create-internet-gateway \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=internet-gateway,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=lemp-igw}]' \
  --query 'InternetGateway.InternetGatewayId' --output text)
aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway --internet-gateway-id $IGW_ID --vpc-id $VPC_ID

# Public subnet (App server lives here)
PUB_SUBNET=$(aws ec2 create-subnet \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block 10.0.1.0/24 \
  --availability-zone us-east-1a \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=lemp-public}]' \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

# Enable auto-assign public IP on public subnet
aws ec2 modify-subnet-attribute --subnet-id $PUB_SUBNET \
  --map-public-ip-on-launch

# Private subnet (MySQL lives here)
PRIV_SUBNET=$(aws ec2 create-subnet \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block 10.0.2.0/24 \
  --availability-zone us-east-1b \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=lemp-private}]' \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

# Public route table → Internet Gateway
RT_ID=$(aws ec2 create-route-table --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --query 'RouteTable.RouteTableId' --output text)
aws ec2 create-route --route-table-id $RT_ID \
  --destination-cidr-block 0.0.0.0/0 --gateway-id $IGW_ID
aws ec2 associate-route-table --route-table-id $RT_ID \
  --subnet-id $PUB_SUBNET

echo "VPC=$VPC_ID  PUB=$PUB_SUBNET  PRIV=$PRIV_SUBNET  IGW=$IGW_ID"

Step 2 — Create Security Groups

# SG for ALB — accepts HTTP/HTTPS from anywhere
ALB_SG=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name lemp-alb-sg \
  --description "ALB Security Group" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --query 'GroupId' --output text)

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $ALB_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 80 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $ALB_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 443 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# SG for App EC2 — accepts HTTP from ALB, SSH from your IP
APP_SG=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name lemp-app-sg \
  --description "App Server Security Group" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --query 'GroupId' --output text)

# HTTP only from ALB SG (not from internet directly)
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 80 \
  --source-group $ALB_SG

# SSH from your IP only — replace with your actual IP
MY_IP=$(curl -s https://checkip.amazonaws.com)
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 22 \
  --cidr "${MY_IP}/32"

# SG for MySQL EC2 — accepts port 3306 only from App SG
DB_SG=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name lemp-db-sg \
  --description "MySQL Security Group" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --query 'GroupId' --output text)

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $DB_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 3306 \
  --source-group $APP_SG

echo "ALB_SG=$ALB_SG  APP_SG=$APP_SG  DB_SG=$DB_SG"

Step 3 — Launch App EC2 (Public Subnet)

User Data Script — installs LEMP stack automatically on boot

# Save as app-userdata.sh
cat > app-userdata.sh << 'USERDATA'
#!/bin/bash
set -e
exec > /var/log/user-data.log 2>&1

# Update system
dnf update -y

# Install Nginx
dnf install -y nginx
systemctl start nginx
systemctl enable nginx

# Install PHP 8.2 + FPM + extensions
dnf install -y php8.2 php8.2-fpm php8.2-mysqlnd \
  php8.2-gd php8.2-mbstring php8.2-xml php8.2-opcache \
  php8.2-curl php8.2-zip
systemctl start php-fpm
systemctl enable php-fpm

# Configure Nginx for PHP
cat > /etc/nginx/conf.d/app.conf << 'NGINXCONF'
server {
    listen 80 default_server;
    root /var/www/html;
    index index.php index.html;

    location / {
        try_files $uri $uri/ /index.php?$query_string;
    }

    location ~ \.php$ {
        fastcgi_pass unix:/run/php-fpm/www.sock;
        fastcgi_index index.php;
        fastcgi_param SCRIPT_FILENAME $document_root$fastcgi_script_name;
        include fastcgi_params;
    }

    location ~ /\.ht {
        deny all;
    }

    add_header X-Frame-Options "SAMEORIGIN";
    add_header X-Content-Type-Options "nosniff";
    add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
    server_tokens off;
}
NGINXCONF

# Remove default nginx config
rm -f /etc/nginx/conf.d/default.conf

# Create test PHP page
cat > /var/www/html/index.php << 'PHPEOF'
<?php
echo "<h1>LEMP Stack Running!</h1>";
echo "<p>Server: " . $_SERVER['SERVER_ADDR'] . "</p>";
phpinfo();
PHPEOF

# Create health check page for ALB
echo "OK" > /var/www/html/health.html

# Fix permissions
chown -R nginx:nginx /var/www/html
chmod -R 755 /var/www/html

# Reload Nginx with new config
nginx -t && systemctl reload nginx
echo "App setup complete" > /tmp/setup-done
USERDATA
# Get latest Amazon Linux 2023 AMI
AMI=$(aws ec2 describe-images \
  --owners amazon \
  --filters "Name=name,Values=al2023-ami-*-x86_64" \
            "Name=state,Values=available" \
  --query 'sort_by(Images,&CreationDate)[-1].ImageId' \
  --output text)

# Launch App EC2
APP_INSTANCE=$(aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id $AMI \
  --instance-type t3.small \
  --key-name YOUR_KEY_PAIR_NAME \
  --subnet-id $PUB_SUBNET \
  --security-group-ids $APP_SG \
  --user-data file://app-userdata.sh \
  --tag-specifications \
    'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=lemp-app},{Key=Role,Value=application}]' \
  --query 'Instances[0].InstanceId' --output text)

echo "App Instance: $APP_INSTANCE"

# Wait for it to be running
aws ec2 wait instance-running --instance-ids $APP_INSTANCE

# Get public IP
APP_PUBLIC_IP=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $APP_INSTANCE \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].PublicIpAddress' \
  --output text)

APP_PRIVATE_IP=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $APP_INSTANCE \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].PrivateIpAddress' \
  --output text)

echo "App Public IP: $APP_PUBLIC_IP"
echo "App Private IP: $APP_PRIVATE_IP"

Step 4 — Launch MySQL EC2 (Private Subnet)

# Save as db-userdata.sh
cat > db-userdata.sh << 'USERDATA'
#!/bin/bash
set -e
exec > /var/log/user-data.log 2>&1

# Update system
dnf update -y

# Install MySQL 8
dnf install -y mysql-server
systemctl start mysqld
systemctl enable mysqld

# Secure MySQL and create app database
mysql -u root << 'MYSQL'
ALTER USER 'root'@'localhost' IDENTIFIED BY 'RootPass@123!';
DELETE FROM mysql.user WHERE User='';
DELETE FROM mysql.user WHERE User='root' AND Host NOT IN ('localhost','127.0.0.1','::1');
DROP DATABASE IF EXISTS test;
DELETE FROM mysql.db WHERE Db='test' OR Db='test\\_%';
CREATE DATABASE appdb CHARACTER SET utf8mb4 COLLATE utf8mb4_unicode_ci;
CREATE USER 'appuser'@'10.0.1.%' IDENTIFIED BY 'AppPass@456!';
GRANT ALL PRIVILEGES ON appdb.* TO 'appuser'@'10.0.1.%';
FLUSH PRIVILEGES;
MYSQL

# Allow MySQL to listen on all interfaces (App can connect from 10.0.1.x)
sed -i 's/^#bind-address.*/bind-address = 0.0.0.0/' /etc/my.cnf.d/mysql-server.cnf
echo "bind-address = 0.0.0.0" >> /etc/my.cnf.d/mysql-server.cnf

systemctl restart mysqld
echo "MySQL setup complete" > /tmp/db-setup-done
USERDATA

# Launch MySQL EC2 in private subnet — NO public IP
DB_INSTANCE=$(aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id $AMI \
  --instance-type t3.small \
  --key-name YOUR_KEY_PAIR_NAME \
  --subnet-id $PRIV_SUBNET \
  --security-group-ids $DB_SG \
  --no-associate-public-ip-address \
  --user-data file://db-userdata.sh \
  --tag-specifications \
    'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=lemp-mysql},{Key=Role,Value=database}]' \
  --query 'Instances[0].InstanceId' --output text)

echo "DB Instance: $DB_INSTANCE"

aws ec2 wait instance-running --instance-ids $DB_INSTANCE

DB_PRIVATE_IP=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $DB_INSTANCE \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].PrivateIpAddress' \
  --output text)

echo "MySQL Private IP: $DB_PRIVATE_IP"

Step 5 — Create Application Load Balancer

# Second public subnet needed for ALB (ALB requires 2 AZs)
PUB_SUBNET_2=$(aws ec2 create-subnet \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block 10.0.3.0/24 \
  --availability-zone us-east-1b \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=lemp-public-2}]' \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

aws ec2 modify-subnet-attribute --subnet-id $PUB_SUBNET_2 \
  --map-public-ip-on-launch
aws ec2 associate-route-table --route-table-id $RT_ID \
  --subnet-id $PUB_SUBNET_2

# Create ALB
ALB_ARN=$(aws elbv2 create-load-balancer \
  --name lemp-alb \
  --subnets $PUB_SUBNET $PUB_SUBNET_2 \
  --security-groups $ALB_SG \
  --scheme internet-facing \
  --type application \
  --ip-address-type ipv4 \
  --tags Key=Name,Value=lemp-alb \
  --query 'LoadBalancers[0].LoadBalancerArn' --output text)

echo "ALB ARN: $ALB_ARN"

# Create Target Group
TG_ARN=$(aws elbv2 create-target-group \
  --name lemp-app-tg \
  --protocol HTTP \
  --port 80 \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --health-check-protocol HTTP \
  --health-check-path /health.html \
  --health-check-interval-seconds 30 \
  --health-check-timeout-seconds 5 \
  --healthy-threshold-count 2 \
  --unhealthy-threshold-count 3 \
  --target-type instance \
  --query 'TargetGroups[0].TargetGroupArn' --output text)

echo "Target Group ARN: $TG_ARN"

# Register App EC2 in Target Group
aws elbv2 register-targets \
  --target-group-arn $TG_ARN \
  --targets Id=$APP_INSTANCE,Port=80

# Create Listener on ALB port 80 → Target Group
aws elbv2 create-listener \
  --load-balancer-arn $ALB_ARN \
  --protocol HTTP \
  --port 80 \
  --default-actions Type=forward,TargetGroupArn=$TG_ARN

# Get ALB DNS name
ALB_DNS=$(aws elbv2 describe-load-balancers \
  --load-balancer-arns $ALB_ARN \
  --query 'LoadBalancers[0].DNSName' --output text)

echo ""
echo "============================================"
echo "ALB DNS: http://$ALB_DNS"
echo "App Public IP (SSH): $APP_PUBLIC_IP"
echo "MySQL Private IP: $DB_PRIVATE_IP"
echo "============================================"

Step 6 — Connect App to MySQL

# SSH into App server
ssh -i ~/.ssh/YOUR_KEY.pem ec2-user@$APP_PUBLIC_IP

# On the app server — test MySQL connectivity
mysql -h 10.0.2.x -u appuser -p'AppPass@456!' appdb -e "SHOW DATABASES;"

# Update your PHP app's DB config
cat > /var/www/html/db-test.php << 'EOF'
<?php
$conn = new mysqli('10.0.2.x', 'appuser', 'AppPass@456!', 'appdb');
if ($conn->connect_error) {
    die("Connection failed: " . $conn->connect_error);
}
echo "Connected to MySQL successfully!";
echo "MySQL version: " . $conn->server_info;
$conn->close();
EOF

Step 7 — Verify Everything

# Check ALB target health
aws elbv2 describe-target-health \
  --target-group-arn $TG_ARN \
  --query 'TargetHealthDescriptions[*].{Target:Target.Id,Health:TargetHealth.State}'

# Expected output:
# [{"Target": "i-0abc...", "Health": "healthy"}]

# Test via ALB
curl -I http://$ALB_DNS
# Expected: HTTP/1.1 200 OK

# SSH access to App (direct)
ssh -i ~/.ssh/YOUR_KEY.pem ec2-user@$APP_PUBLIC_IP
# MySQL EC2 has NO public IP — can only be reached from App server
Expected result:
• http://<ALB-DNS> loads the PHP page via ALB
• ssh ec2-user@<APP-PUBLIC-IP> works (direct access)
• MySQL EC2 has no public IP — zero internet exposure
• Port 3306 reachable only from App server's private IP

Cleanup (avoid charges)

# Delete in reverse order
aws elbv2 delete-listener --listener-arn $LISTENER_ARN
aws elbv2 delete-target-group --target-group-arn $TG_ARN
aws elbv2 delete-load-balancer --load-balancer-arn $ALB_ARN
aws ec2 terminate-instances --instance-ids $APP_INSTANCE $DB_INSTANCE
aws ec2 wait instance-terminated --instance-ids $APP_INSTANCE $DB_INSTANCE
# Then delete SGs, subnets, route tables, IGW, VPC
ALB costs ~$0.008/hour even when idle. Always delete after practice sessions. Use AWS Budgets to set a $10/month alert.

Interview Questions — This Setup

Why is the MySQL instance in a private subnet with no public IP?
Security principle of least exposure — the database should never be directly reachable from the internet. A public IP means anyone can attempt connections on port 3306 (brute-force, credential stuffing). In the private subnet with DB security group allowing port 3306 only from the App security group, only the application server can reach MySQL — even if an attacker compromises another service, they cannot reach the DB directly. Defense in depth: network isolation is the first layer, strong passwords and IAM are additional layers.
Why use ALB instead of pointing DNS directly to the App EC2 public IP?
1) Scalability: ALB can route to multiple app servers (Auto Scaling Group) — direct IP only reaches one. 2) Health checks: ALB stops sending traffic to unhealthy instances automatically. 3) SSL termination: ACM certificate attached to ALB handles HTTPS — instances serve plain HTTP internally. 4) Fixed endpoint: EC2 public IPs change on restart; ALB DNS name is stable. 5) Security: App SG allows port 80 only from ALB SG — EC2 is never directly internet-accessible even though it's in a public subnet.
🏛️

Project 5 — Full Production Multi-Tier AWS Architecture with Bastion

Advanced

A hardened, highly-available production setup: multiple app servers behind an ALB, a dedicated Bastion host as the sole SSH entry point, MySQL in a private subnet, and all servers properly segmented with security groups and private networking.

Architecture Overview

Internet │ ┌──────────────┴──────────────┐ │ Application Load Balancer │ ← internet-facing │ (port 80 / 443) │ └──────┬───────────────┬───────┘ │ │ ┌───────────▼───────────────▼───────────┐ │ VPC 10.0.0.0/16 │ │ │ │ ┌─────────────────────────────────┐ │ │ │ Public Subnets (2 AZs) │ │ │ │ 10.0.1.0/24 10.0.2.0/24 │ │ │ │ │ │ │ │ ┌─────────┐ ┌───────────────┐ │ │ │ │ │ Bastion │ │ NAT Gateway │ │ │ ← SSH entry point │ │ │ Host │ │ (AZ-a + AZ-b)│ │ │ only server with │ │ │(t3.nano)│ │ │ │ │ port 22 open to │ │ └────┬────┘ └───────────────┘ │ │ internet │ └───────│─────────────────────────-─┘ │ │ │ SSH only │ │ ┌───────▼──────────────────────────┐ │ │ │ Private App Subnets (2 AZs) │ │ │ │ 10.0.11.0/24 10.0.12.0/24 │ │ │ │ │ │ │ │ ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────────┐ │ │ │ │ │ App-1 │ │ App-2 │ │ │ │ │ │ (Nginx + │ │ (Nginx + │ │ │ │ │ │ PHP-FPM)│ │ PHP-FPM) │ │ │ │ │ └──────────┘ └──────────────┘ │ │ │ └───────────────────┬───────────────┘ │ │ │ port 3306 │ │ ┌───────────────────▼───────────────┐ │ │ │ Private DB Subnets (2 AZs) │ │ │ │ 10.0.21.0/24 10.0.22.0/24 │ │ │ │ │ │ │ │ ┌──────────┐ ┌────────────────┐ │ │ │ │ │ MySQL │ │ MySQL Replica │ │ │ (optional read replica) │ │ │ Primary │ │ (standby) │ │ │ │ │ └──────────┘ └────────────────┘ │ │ │ └────────────────────────────────────┘ │ └────────────────────────────────────────────┘
This architecture follows AWS Well-Architected Framework: Security, Reliability, Performance Efficiency, Cost Optimization, Operational Excellence. Used in real-world SaaS, e-commerce, and enterprise apps.

What Each Component Does

ComponentSubnetPublic IPPurpose
ALBPublic (both AZs)Yes (managed)Receives all user traffic, distributes to App servers
Bastion HostPublic (AZ-a)Yes (Elastic IP)Only SSH gateway — you SSH here first, then jump to private servers
NAT GatewayPublic (each AZ)Yes (Elastic IP)Lets private servers reach internet (updates, packages) — no inbound
App Server 1 & 2Private AppNoRun Nginx + PHP-FPM, serve application
MySQL PrimaryPrivate DBNoAccepts writes, primary database

Step 1 — VPC with Full Subnet Layout

#!/bin/bash
set -e

REGION="us-east-1"
PROJECT="prod"

# Create VPC
VPC_ID=$(aws ec2 create-vpc \
  --cidr-block 10.0.0.0/16 --region $REGION \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=vpc,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-vpc}]" \
  --query 'Vpc.VpcId' --output text)

aws ec2 modify-vpc-attribute --vpc-id $VPC_ID --enable-dns-hostnames '{"Value":true}'
aws ec2 modify-vpc-attribute --vpc-id $VPC_ID --enable-dns-support '{"Value":true}'

# Internet Gateway
IGW_ID=$(aws ec2 create-internet-gateway \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=internet-gateway,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-igw}]" \
  --query 'InternetGateway.InternetGatewayId' --output text)
aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway --internet-gateway-id $IGW_ID --vpc-id $VPC_ID

# ── Public Subnets ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
PUB_A=$(aws ec2 create-subnet --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block 10.0.1.0/24 --availability-zone ${REGION}a \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-public-a}]" \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

PUB_B=$(aws ec2 create-subnet --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block 10.0.2.0/24 --availability-zone ${REGION}b \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-public-b}]" \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

aws ec2 modify-subnet-attribute --subnet-id $PUB_A --map-public-ip-on-launch
aws ec2 modify-subnet-attribute --subnet-id $PUB_B --map-public-ip-on-launch

# ── Private App Subnets ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────
APP_A=$(aws ec2 create-subnet --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block 10.0.11.0/24 --availability-zone ${REGION}a \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-app-a}]" \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

APP_B=$(aws ec2 create-subnet --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block 10.0.12.0/24 --availability-zone ${REGION}b \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-app-b}]" \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

# ── Private DB Subnets ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────
DB_A=$(aws ec2 create-subnet --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block 10.0.21.0/24 --availability-zone ${REGION}a \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-db-a}]" \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

DB_B=$(aws ec2 create-subnet --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block 10.0.22.0/24 --availability-zone ${REGION}b \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-db-b}]" \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

echo "Subnets created: PUB_A=$PUB_A PUB_B=$PUB_B APP_A=$APP_A APP_B=$APP_B DB_A=$DB_A DB_B=$DB_B"

Step 2 — NAT Gateways + Route Tables

# Elastic IPs for NAT Gateways
EIP_A=$(aws ec2 allocate-address --domain vpc \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=elastic-ip,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-nat-eip-a}]" \
  --query 'AllocationId' --output text)

EIP_B=$(aws ec2 allocate-address --domain vpc \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=elastic-ip,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-nat-eip-b}]" \
  --query 'AllocationId' --output text)

# Create NAT Gateways in each public subnet (HA — one per AZ)
NAT_A=$(aws ec2 create-nat-gateway \
  --subnet-id $PUB_A --allocation-id $EIP_A \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=natgateway,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-nat-a}]" \
  --query 'NatGateway.NatGatewayId' --output text)

NAT_B=$(aws ec2 create-nat-gateway \
  --subnet-id $PUB_B --allocation-id $EIP_B \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=natgateway,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-nat-b}]" \
  --query 'NatGateway.NatGatewayId' --output text)

echo "Waiting for NAT Gateways to be available..."
aws ec2 wait nat-gateway-available --nat-gateway-ids $NAT_A $NAT_B

# ── Public Route Table (→ IGW) ───────────────────────────────────────────────
PUB_RT=$(aws ec2 create-route-table --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=route-table,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-rt-public}]" \
  --query 'RouteTable.RouteTableId' --output text)
aws ec2 create-route --route-table-id $PUB_RT \
  --destination-cidr-block 0.0.0.0/0 --gateway-id $IGW_ID
aws ec2 associate-route-table --route-table-id $PUB_RT --subnet-id $PUB_A
aws ec2 associate-route-table --route-table-id $PUB_RT --subnet-id $PUB_B

# ── Private Route Tables (→ NAT, one per AZ for HA) ─────────────────────────
PRIV_RT_A=$(aws ec2 create-route-table --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=route-table,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-rt-private-a}]" \
  --query 'RouteTable.RouteTableId' --output text)
aws ec2 create-route --route-table-id $PRIV_RT_A \
  --destination-cidr-block 0.0.0.0/0 --nat-gateway-id $NAT_A
aws ec2 associate-route-table --route-table-id $PRIV_RT_A --subnet-id $APP_A
aws ec2 associate-route-table --route-table-id $PRIV_RT_A --subnet-id $DB_A

PRIV_RT_B=$(aws ec2 create-route-table --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=route-table,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-rt-private-b}]" \
  --query 'RouteTable.RouteTableId' --output text)
aws ec2 create-route --route-table-id $PRIV_RT_B \
  --destination-cidr-block 0.0.0.0/0 --nat-gateway-id $NAT_B
aws ec2 associate-route-table --route-table-id $PRIV_RT_B --subnet-id $APP_B
aws ec2 associate-route-table --route-table-id $PRIV_RT_B --subnet-id $DB_B

echo "Route tables done"

Step 3 — Security Groups (Full Ruleset)

MY_IP=$(curl -s https://checkip.amazonaws.com)

# ── Bastion SG — SSH only from your IP ───────────────────────────────────────
BASTION_SG=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name ${PROJECT}-bastion-sg \
  --description "Bastion Host - SSH only from admin IP" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID --query 'GroupId' --output text)

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress --group-id $BASTION_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 22 --cidr "${MY_IP}/32"

# ── ALB SG — HTTP/HTTPS from internet ────────────────────────────────────────
ALB_SG=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name ${PROJECT}-alb-sg \
  --description "ALB - HTTP/HTTPS from internet" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID --query 'GroupId' --output text)

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress --group-id $ALB_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 80 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress --group-id $ALB_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 443 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# ── App SG — HTTP from ALB, SSH from Bastion only ────────────────────────────
APP_SG=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name ${PROJECT}-app-sg \
  --description "App Servers - HTTP from ALB, SSH from Bastion" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID --query 'GroupId' --output text)

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 80 --source-group $ALB_SG

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 22 --source-group $BASTION_SG

# ── DB SG — MySQL from App servers only ──────────────────────────────────────
DB_SG=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name ${PROJECT}-db-sg \
  --description "MySQL - port 3306 from App SG only" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID --query 'GroupId' --output text)

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress --group-id $DB_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 3306 --source-group $APP_SG

# Also allow Bastion to SSH into DB server for maintenance
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress --group-id $DB_SG \
  --protocol tcp --port 22 --source-group $BASTION_SG

echo "Security Groups: BASTION=$BASTION_SG ALB=$ALB_SG APP=$APP_SG DB=$DB_SG"

Step 4 — Launch Bastion Host

# Bastion = tiny instance, only for SSH tunneling — no app runs here
AMI=$(aws ec2 describe-images \
  --owners amazon \
  --filters "Name=name,Values=al2023-ami-*-x86_64" \
            "Name=state,Values=available" \
  --query 'sort_by(Images,&CreationDate)[-1].ImageId' \
  --output text)

BASTION=$(aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id $AMI \
  --instance-type t3.nano \
  --key-name YOUR_KEY_PAIR_NAME \
  --subnet-id $PUB_A \
  --security-group-ids $BASTION_SG \
  --tag-specifications \
    "ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-bastion}]" \
  --query 'Instances[0].InstanceId' --output text)

aws ec2 wait instance-running --instance-ids $BASTION

# Assign Elastic IP to Bastion (static IP — doesn't change on restart)
BASTION_EIP=$(aws ec2 allocate-address --domain vpc \
  --query 'AllocationId' --output text)
aws ec2 associate-address \
  --instance-id $BASTION \
  --allocation-id $BASTION_EIP

BASTION_IP=$(aws ec2 describe-addresses \
  --allocation-ids $BASTION_EIP \
  --query 'Addresses[0].PublicIp' --output text)

echo "Bastion IP: $BASTION_IP  (SSH: ssh -i key.pem ec2-user@$BASTION_IP)"

Step 5 — Launch App Servers (Private Subnets)

# App user-data — same LEMP install from Setup 1
cat > app-userdata.sh << 'USERDATA'
#!/bin/bash
set -e
exec > /var/log/user-data.log 2>&1
dnf update -y
dnf install -y nginx php8.2 php8.2-fpm php8.2-mysqlnd \
  php8.2-gd php8.2-mbstring php8.2-opcache php8.2-curl php8.2-zip

systemctl start nginx php-fpm
systemctl enable nginx php-fpm

cat > /etc/nginx/conf.d/app.conf << 'NGINXCONF'
server {
    listen 80 default_server;
    root /var/www/html;
    index index.php index.html;
    location / { try_files $uri $uri/ /index.php?$query_string; }
    location ~ \.php$ {
        fastcgi_pass unix:/run/php-fpm/www.sock;
        include fastcgi_params;
        fastcgi_param SCRIPT_FILENAME $document_root$fastcgi_script_name;
    }
    server_tokens off;
}
NGINXCONF

rm -f /etc/nginx/conf.d/default.conf
echo "<?php echo 'App: ' . gethostname(); ?>" > /var/www/html/index.php
echo "OK" > /var/www/html/health.html
chown -R nginx:nginx /var/www/html
nginx -t && systemctl reload nginx
USERDATA

# App Server 1 — AZ-a private subnet
APP1=$(aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id $AMI \
  --instance-type t3.small \
  --key-name YOUR_KEY_PAIR_NAME \
  --subnet-id $APP_A \
  --security-group-ids $APP_SG \
  --no-associate-public-ip-address \
  --user-data file://app-userdata.sh \
  --tag-specifications \
    "ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-app-1},{Key=Role,Value=app}]" \
  --query 'Instances[0].InstanceId' --output text)

# App Server 2 — AZ-b private subnet
APP2=$(aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id $AMI \
  --instance-type t3.small \
  --key-name YOUR_KEY_PAIR_NAME \
  --subnet-id $APP_B \
  --security-group-ids $APP_SG \
  --no-associate-public-ip-address \
  --user-data file://app-userdata.sh \
  --tag-specifications \
    "ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-app-2},{Key=Role,Value=app}]" \
  --query 'Instances[0].InstanceId' --output text)

aws ec2 wait instance-running --instance-ids $APP1 $APP2
APP1_IP=$(aws ec2 describe-instances --instance-ids $APP1 \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].PrivateIpAddress' --output text)
APP2_IP=$(aws ec2 describe-instances --instance-ids $APP2 \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].PrivateIpAddress' --output text)
echo "App1 private: $APP1_IP  App2 private: $APP2_IP"

Step 6 — Launch MySQL Server (Private DB Subnet)

# db-userdata.sh — same as Setup 1
cat > db-userdata.sh << 'USERDATA'
#!/bin/bash
set -e
exec > /var/log/user-data.log 2>&1
dnf update -y
dnf install -y mysql-server
systemctl start mysqld
systemctl enable mysqld

mysql -u root << 'MYSQL'
ALTER USER 'root'@'localhost' IDENTIFIED BY 'RootPass@123!';
CREATE DATABASE appdb CHARACTER SET utf8mb4 COLLATE utf8mb4_unicode_ci;
CREATE USER 'appuser'@'10.0.11.%' IDENTIFIED BY 'AppPass@456!';
CREATE USER 'appuser'@'10.0.12.%' IDENTIFIED BY 'AppPass@456!';
GRANT ALL PRIVILEGES ON appdb.* TO 'appuser'@'10.0.11.%';
GRANT ALL PRIVILEGES ON appdb.* TO 'appuser'@'10.0.12.%';
FLUSH PRIVILEGES;
MYSQL

echo "bind-address = 0.0.0.0" >> /etc/my.cnf.d/mysql-server.cnf
systemctl restart mysqld
USERDATA

DB1=$(aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id $AMI \
  --instance-type t3.medium \
  --key-name YOUR_KEY_PAIR_NAME \
  --subnet-id $DB_A \
  --security-group-ids $DB_SG \
  --no-associate-public-ip-address \
  --user-data file://db-userdata.sh \
  --block-device-mappings '[{"DeviceName":"/dev/xvda","Ebs":{"VolumeSize":100,"VolumeType":"gp3","Encrypted":true}}]' \
  --tag-specifications \
    "ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-mysql-primary},{Key=Role,Value=database}]" \
  --query 'Instances[0].InstanceId' --output text)

aws ec2 wait instance-running --instance-ids $DB1
DB1_IP=$(aws ec2 describe-instances --instance-ids $DB1 \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].PrivateIpAddress' --output text)
echo "MySQL Primary IP: $DB1_IP"

Step 7 — Create ALB + Target Group + Listener

# Create ALB in both public subnets
ALB_ARN=$(aws elbv2 create-load-balancer \
  --name ${PROJECT}-alb \
  --subnets $PUB_A $PUB_B \
  --security-groups $ALB_SG \
  --scheme internet-facing \
  --type application \
  --tags Key=Name,Value=${PROJECT}-alb \
  --query 'LoadBalancers[0].LoadBalancerArn' --output text)

# Target Group pointing to App instances
TG_ARN=$(aws elbv2 create-target-group \
  --name ${PROJECT}-app-tg \
  --protocol HTTP --port 80 \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --health-check-path /health.html \
  --health-check-interval-seconds 15 \
  --healthy-threshold-count 2 \
  --unhealthy-threshold-count 3 \
  --target-type instance \
  --query 'TargetGroups[0].TargetGroupArn' --output text)

# Sticky sessions (optional — useful for PHP session-based apps)
aws elbv2 modify-target-group-attributes \
  --target-group-arn $TG_ARN \
  --attributes \
    Key=stickiness.enabled,Value=true \
    Key=stickiness.type,Value=lb_cookie \
    Key=stickiness.lb_cookie.duration_seconds,Value=86400

# Register both app servers
aws elbv2 register-targets \
  --target-group-arn $TG_ARN \
  --targets Id=$APP1,Port=80 Id=$APP2,Port=80

# HTTP Listener — port 80
LISTENER_ARN=$(aws elbv2 create-listener \
  --load-balancer-arn $ALB_ARN \
  --protocol HTTP --port 80 \
  --default-actions Type=forward,TargetGroupArn=$TG_ARN \
  --query 'Listeners[0].ListenerArn' --output text)

ALB_DNS=$(aws elbv2 describe-load-balancers \
  --load-balancer-arns $ALB_ARN \
  --query 'LoadBalancers[0].DNSName' --output text)

echo ""
echo "======================================================"
echo "  PRODUCTION SETUP COMPLETE"
echo "======================================================"
echo "  ALB URL   : http://$ALB_DNS"
echo "  Bastion   : ssh -i key.pem ec2-user@$BASTION_IP"
echo "  App1 (prv): $APP1_IP"
echo "  App2 (prv): $APP2_IP"
echo "  MySQL(prv): $DB1_IP"
echo "======================================================"

Step 8 — SSH Access via Bastion (Jump Host)

# Method 1: Manual jump
# First SSH to Bastion, then from Bastion SSH to private server
ssh -i ~/.ssh/prod-key.pem ec2-user@$BASTION_IP         # step 1: enter bastion
ssh -i ~/.ssh/prod-key.pem ec2-user@$APP1_IP            # step 2: from bastion to app

# Method 2: SSH ProxyJump (one command from your laptop)
ssh -i ~/.ssh/prod-key.pem \
    -J ec2-user@$BASTION_IP \
    ec2-user@$APP1_IP

# Method 3: ~/.ssh/config (recommended — saves typing every time)
cat >> ~/.ssh/config << EOF
Host bastion
  HostName $BASTION_IP
  User ec2-user
  IdentityFile ~/.ssh/prod-key.pem
  StrictHostKeyChecking no

Host prod-app1
  HostName $APP1_IP
  User ec2-user
  IdentityFile ~/.ssh/prod-key.pem
  ProxyJump bastion

Host prod-app2
  HostName $APP2_IP
  User ec2-user
  IdentityFile ~/.ssh/prod-key.pem
  ProxyJump bastion

Host prod-mysql
  HostName $DB1_IP
  User ec2-user
  IdentityFile ~/.ssh/prod-key.pem
  ProxyJump bastion
EOF

# Now you can simply run:
ssh prod-app1
ssh prod-mysql

# Port-forward MySQL to your local machine for GUI tools (DBeaver, TablePlus)
ssh -L 3306:$DB1_IP:3306 bastion -N &
# Then connect localhost:3306 in your DB client

Step 9 — Verify Full Stack

# Check ALB target health
aws elbv2 describe-target-health \
  --target-group-arn $TG_ARN \
  --query 'TargetHealthDescriptions[*].{ID:Target.Id,State:TargetHealth.State,Reason:TargetHealth.Reason}'

# Expected:
# [{"ID": "i-0app1", "State": "healthy"}, {"ID": "i-0app2", "State": "healthy"}]

# Test ALB distributes to both app servers
for i in {1..6}; do
  curl -s http://$ALB_DNS/ | grep -o 'App: [^<]*'
done
# Should alternate between App1 hostname and App2 hostname

# From App server — test MySQL
ssh prod-app1
mysql -h $DB1_IP -u appuser -p'AppPass@456!' appdb -e "SELECT 'DB connection OK';"

# Verify no public access to private instances
curl --connect-timeout 5 http://$APP1_IP || echo "Correctly unreachable from internet"

Step 10 — Add HTTPS with ACM Certificate

# Request free SSL certificate (domain must exist in Route 53 or be verified)
CERT_ARN=$(aws acm request-certificate \
  --domain-name "yourdomain.com" \
  --validation-method DNS \
  --subject-alternative-names "www.yourdomain.com" \
  --query 'CertificateArn' --output text)

# After DNS validation (add the CNAME records ACM shows you):
# Create HTTPS listener on ALB
aws elbv2 create-listener \
  --load-balancer-arn $ALB_ARN \
  --protocol HTTPS --port 443 \
  --certificates CertificateArn=$CERT_ARN \
  --ssl-policy ELBSecurityPolicy-TLS13-1-2-2021-06 \
  --default-actions Type=forward,TargetGroupArn=$TG_ARN

# Redirect HTTP → HTTPS on port 80 listener
aws elbv2 modify-listener \
  --listener-arn $LISTENER_ARN \
  --default-actions \
    Type=redirect,RedirectConfig='{Protocol=HTTPS,Port=443,StatusCode=HTTP_301}'

# Create Route 53 alias record → ALB
aws route53 change-resource-record-sets \
  --hosted-zone-id YOUR_ZONE_ID \
  --change-batch '{
    "Changes": [{
      "Action": "UPSERT",
      "ResourceRecordSet": {
        "Name": "yourdomain.com",
        "Type": "A",
        "AliasTarget": {
          "HostedZoneId": "Z35SXDOTRQ7X7K",
          "DNSName": "'$ALB_DNS'",
          "EvaluateTargetHealth": true
        }
      }
    }]
  }'
Final state:
• All traffic enters via ALB → distributed across 2 App servers (2 AZs = HA)
• Zero direct internet access to App or DB servers
• Only one public entry point for SSH: Bastion with Elastic IP
• MySQL reachable only from App server private IPs via port 3306
• HTTPS with ACM cert at no extra cost
• App servers can reach internet (package updates) via NAT Gateway — no inbound

Security Group Flow Summary

Internet │ ├──:80/:443──→ ALB-SG (allows all inbound 80/443) │ │ │ └──:80──→ APP-SG (allows 80 from ALB-SG only) │ │ │ └──:3306──→ DB-SG (allows 3306 from APP-SG only) │ └──:22──→ BASTION-SG (allows 22 from YOUR_IP only) │ └──:22──→ APP-SG (allows 22 from BASTION-SG) └──:22──→ DB-SG (allows 22 from BASTION-SG)

Interview Questions — This Setup

What is a Bastion host and why do you use it instead of direct SSH?
A Bastion (jump host) is a hardened EC2 instance in a public subnet whose sole purpose is to be an SSH entry point. Benefits: 1) Single audit point — all admin access goes through one server, making it easy to log and monitor. 2) Reduced attack surface — private servers have no public IPs, so they can't be port-scanned or brute-forced from the internet. 3) Fine-grained control — you whitelist only specific admin IPs on the Bastion SG. 4) Compliance — many standards (PCI-DSS, SOC2) require isolated admin access paths. Alternative: AWS Systems Manager Session Manager removes the need for a Bastion entirely (no SSH keys, no open ports, full audit trail).
Why have NAT Gateways if private servers can't be accessed from internet?
NAT Gateway provides outbound-only internet access for private instances. Private servers still need to reach the internet for: installing OS updates (dnf update), pulling Docker images, downloading application packages, calling external APIs (payment gateways, SMS services), sending CloudWatch metrics. Without NAT Gateway, private instances are completely isolated — even dnf update -y would fail. NAT Gateway allows outbound traffic but blocks all unsolicited inbound connections (it does network address translation, not port forwarding).
How would you make this architecture more resilient against AZ failures?
The architecture already handles AZ failures if set up correctly: 1) ALB is multi-AZ — if AZ-a fails, it routes 100% to App-2 in AZ-b automatically. 2) Two NAT Gateways (one per AZ) — each private route table routes through its AZ's NAT. 3) MySQL becomes the single point of failure — fix with: RDS Multi-AZ (synchronous standby in AZ-b, automatic failover in ~60s), or MySQL with read replica promoted manually. Also add Auto Scaling Group across both app subnets — replaces failed instances automatically. With this, the architecture survives full AZ loss with zero manual intervention.
How do you deploy a code update to both app servers without downtime?
Rolling deployment: 1) Deregister App-1 from ALB target group (ALB stops sending traffic to it, existing connections drain). 2) SSH via Bastion to App-1, pull new code, restart services, run smoke test. 3) Re-register App-1 in ALB, wait for health check to pass. 4) Repeat for App-2. Zero downtime because App-2 handles all traffic during App-1 update. Automate this with: an Ansible playbook with serial: 1 (update one at a time), or CodeDeploy with in-place deployment and ALB integration (handles deregistration/registration automatically).
☁️

Project 6 — Cloudflare CDN + WAF + Terraform-managed AWS ALB

Advanced

Provision a complete, production-grade web stack entirely through Terraform: AWS VPC, EC2 Auto Scaling Group, Application Load Balancer, ACM certificate — and then sit Cloudflare in front as the CDN, WAF, and DDoS shield. Zero manual clicks.

Architecture Overview

User → Cloudflare Edge (150+ PoPs worldwide) │ CDN cache / WAF rules / DDoS protection / Rate limiting │ SSL terminates at Cloudflare (Full-Strict mode) ▼ AWS ALB (HTTPS :443, ACM cert — origin cert) │ health checks, sticky sessions ┌──────┴──────┐ ▼ ▼ EC2 App-1 EC2 App-2 ← Auto Scaling Group (private subnets) (Nginx+PHP) (Nginx+PHP) │ ▼ MySQL RDS (Multi-AZ, private) Cloudflare → ALB only accepts traffic from Cloudflare IPs (origin protection) Terraform manages: VPC, subnets, SGs, ALB, ASG, ACM, Route53, Cloudflare DNS/WAF
Cloudflare sits between users and your AWS ALB — users never see your ALB IP. This gives you free DDoS protection, WAF, CDN caching, and Bot management at the edge before traffic hits your infra.

Project Structure

terraform-cloudflare-alb/
├── main.tf
├── variables.tf
├── outputs.tf
├── terraform.tfvars
├── modules/
│   ├── vpc/
│   │   ├── main.tf

│   ├── alb/
│   │   ├── main.tf
│   │   └── outputs.tf
│   ├── asg/
│   │   ├── main.tf

│   │   └── outputs.tf
│   ├── rds/
│   │   ├── main.tf
│   │   └── outputs.tf

Root main.tf — Wiring all modules

terraform {
  required_version = ">= 1.7.0"
  required_providers {
    aws = {
      source  = "hashicorp/aws"
      version = "~> 5.0"
    }
    cloudflare = {
      source  = "cloudflare/cloudflare"
      version = "~> 4.0"
    }
    random = { source = "hashicorp/random" }
  }
  backend "s3" {
    bucket         = "my-tf-state-bucket"
    key            = "prod/cloudflare-alb/terraform.tfstate"
    region         = "us-east-1"
    dynamodb_table = "terraform-locks"
    encrypt        = true
  }
}

provider "aws" {
  region = var.aws_region
  default_tags {
    tags = {
      Project     = var.project
      Environment = var.environment
      ManagedBy   = "Terraform"
    }
  }
}

provider "cloudflare" {
  api_token = var.cloudflare_api_token
}

# ── VPC ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
module "vpc" {
  source = "./modules/vpc"

  project     = var.project
  environment = var.environment
  vpc_cidr    = "10.0.0.0/16"

  public_subnets  = ["10.0.1.0/24", "10.0.2.0/24"]
  private_subnets = ["10.0.11.0/24", "10.0.12.0/24"]
  db_subnets      = ["10.0.21.0/24", "10.0.22.0/24"]
  azs             = ["${var.aws_region}a", "${var.aws_region}b"]
}

# ── ACM Certificate (origin cert for ALB) ────────────────────────────────────
resource "aws_acm_certificate" "origin" {
  domain_name       = var.domain_name
  validation_method = "DNS"

  subject_alternative_names = ["www.${var.domain_name}"]

  lifecycle { create_before_destroy = true }
}

# Auto-validate via Cloudflare DNS records
resource "cloudflare_record" "acm_validation" {
  for_each = {
    for dvo in aws_acm_certificate.origin.domain_validation_options :
    dvo.domain_name => dvo
  }

  zone_id = var.cloudflare_zone_id
  name    = trimsuffix(each.value.resource_record_name, ".")
  type    = each.value.resource_record_type
  value   = trimsuffix(each.value.resource_record_value, ".")
  ttl     = 60
  proxied = false   # must be DNS-only for ACM validation
}

resource "aws_acm_certificate_validation" "origin" {
  certificate_arn         = aws_acm_certificate.origin.arn
  validation_record_fqdns = [for r in cloudflare_record.acm_validation : r.hostname]
}

# ── ALB ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
module "alb" {
  source = "./modules/alb"

  project          = var.project
  environment      = var.environment
  vpc_id           = module.vpc.vpc_id
  public_subnet_ids = module.vpc.public_subnet_ids
  certificate_arn  = aws_acm_certificate.origin.arn

  # Critical: only allow traffic from Cloudflare IP ranges (origin protection)
  cloudflare_ipv4_ranges = var.cloudflare_ipv4_ranges
  cloudflare_ipv6_ranges = var.cloudflare_ipv6_ranges

  depends_on = [aws_acm_certificate_validation.origin]
}

# ── Auto Scaling Group ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
module "asg" {
  source = "./modules/asg"

  project             = var.project
  environment         = var.environment
  vpc_id              = module.vpc.vpc_id
  private_subnet_ids  = module.vpc.private_subnet_ids
  target_group_arn    = module.alb.target_group_arn
  alb_sg_id           = module.alb.alb_sg_id
  db_endpoint         = module.rds.endpoint
  db_secret_arn       = module.rds.secret_arn
  instance_type       = var.instance_type
  key_name            = var.key_name
  min_size            = var.asg_min
  max_size            = var.asg_max
  desired_capacity    = var.asg_desired
}

# ── RDS ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
module "rds" {
  source = "./modules/rds"

  project        = var.project
  environment    = var.environment
  vpc_id         = module.vpc.vpc_id
  db_subnet_ids  = module.vpc.db_subnet_ids
  app_sg_id      = module.asg.app_sg_id
  db_name        = var.db_name
  db_username    = var.db_username
  engine_version = "8.0"
  instance_class = "db.t3.medium"
  multi_az       = var.environment == "prod"
}

# ── Cloudflare ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
module "cloudflare" {
  source = "./modules/cloudflare"

  zone_id      = var.cloudflare_zone_id
  domain_name  = var.domain_name
  alb_dns_name = module.alb.dns_name
  environment  = var.environment
}

modules/alb/main.tf — ALB locked to Cloudflare IPs

# ALB Security Group — ONLY Cloudflare IP ranges (origin protection)
resource "aws_security_group" "alb" {
  name   = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-alb-sg"
  vpc_id = var.vpc_id

  # Cloudflare IPv4 ranges — port 80
  dynamic "ingress" {
    for_each = var.cloudflare_ipv4_ranges
    content {
      from_port   = 80
      to_port     = 80
      protocol    = "tcp"
      cidr_blocks = [ingress.value]
      description = "Cloudflare IPv4"
    }
  }

  # Cloudflare IPv4 ranges — port 443
  dynamic "ingress" {
    for_each = var.cloudflare_ipv4_ranges
    content {
      from_port   = 443
      to_port     = 443
      protocol    = "tcp"
      cidr_blocks = [ingress.value]
      description = "Cloudflare IPv4 HTTPS"
    }
  }

  egress {
    from_port   = 0
    to_port     = 0
    protocol    = "-1"
    cidr_blocks = ["0.0.0.0/0"]
  }
}

resource "aws_lb" "main" {
  name               = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-alb"
  internal           = false
  load_balancer_type = "application"
  security_groups    = [aws_security_group.alb.id]
  subnets            = var.public_subnet_ids

  enable_deletion_protection = var.environment == "prod"
  drop_invalid_header_fields = true   # security best practice

  access_logs {
    bucket  = aws_s3_bucket.alb_logs.id
    prefix  = "${var.project}-alb"
    enabled = true
  }
}

resource "aws_lb_target_group" "app" {
  name     = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-app-tg"
  port     = 80
  protocol = "HTTP"
  vpc_id   = var.vpc_id

  health_check {
    path                = "/health"
    interval            = 15
    timeout             = 5
    healthy_threshold   = 2
    unhealthy_threshold = 3
    matcher             = "200"
  }

  stickiness {
    type            = "lb_cookie"
    cookie_duration = 86400
    enabled         = false   # stateless apps don't need this
  }
}

# HTTP → HTTPS redirect
resource "aws_lb_listener" "http" {
  load_balancer_arn = aws_lb.main.arn
  port              = 80
  protocol          = "HTTP"

  default_action {
    type = "redirect"
    redirect {
      port        = "443"
      protocol    = "HTTPS"
      status_code = "HTTP_301"
    }
  }
}

# HTTPS listener with ACM cert
resource "aws_lb_listener" "https" {
  load_balancer_arn = aws_lb.main.arn
  port              = 443
  protocol          = "HTTPS"
  ssl_policy        = "ELBSecurityPolicy-TLS13-1-2-2021-06"
  certificate_arn   = var.certificate_arn

  default_action {
    type             = "forward"
    target_group_arn = aws_lb_target_group.app.arn
  }
}

# S3 bucket for ALB access logs
resource "aws_s3_bucket" "alb_logs" {
  bucket = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-alb-logs-${random_id.suffix.hex}"
  force_destroy = var.environment != "prod"
}

resource "random_id" "suffix" { byte_length = 4 }

modules/asg/main.tf — Auto Scaling Group

# Launch Template
resource "aws_launch_template" "app" {
  name_prefix   = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-"
  image_id      = data.aws_ami.amazon_linux.id
  instance_type = var.instance_type
  key_name      = var.key_name

  vpc_security_group_ids = [aws_security_group.app.id]

  iam_instance_profile {
    name = aws_iam_instance_profile.app.name
  }

  block_device_mappings {
    device_name = "/dev/xvda"
    ebs {
      volume_size           = 30
      volume_type           = "gp3"
      encrypted             = true
      delete_on_termination = true
    }
  }

  metadata_options {
    http_tokens   = "required"   # enforce IMDSv2
    http_endpoint = "enabled"
  }

  user_data = base64encode(templatefile("${path.module}/userdata.sh.tpl", {
    db_endpoint   = var.db_endpoint
    db_secret_arn = var.db_secret_arn
    environment   = var.environment
  }))

  tag_specifications {
    resource_type = "instance"
    tags = { Name = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-app" }
  }

  lifecycle { create_before_destroy = true }
}

data "aws_ami" "amazon_linux" {
  most_recent = true
  owners      = ["amazon"]
  filter { name = "name";  values = ["al2023-ami-*-x86_64"] }
  filter { name = "state"; values = ["available"] }
}

# Auto Scaling Group
resource "aws_autoscaling_group" "app" {
  name                = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-asg"
  min_size            = var.min_size
  max_size            = var.max_size
  desired_capacity    = var.desired_capacity
  vpc_zone_identifier = var.private_subnet_ids
  target_group_arns   = [var.target_group_arn]
  health_check_type   = "ELB"
  health_check_grace_period = 120

  launch_template {
    id      = aws_launch_template.app.id
    version = "$Latest"
  }

  instance_refresh {
    strategy = "Rolling"
    preferences {
      min_healthy_percentage = 50
      instance_warmup        = 60
    }
  }

  dynamic "tag" {
    for_each = {
      Name        = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-app"
      Environment = var.environment
    }
    content {
      key                 = tag.key
      value               = tag.value
      propagate_at_launch = true
    }
  }
}

# Target tracking — keep CPU at 60%
resource "aws_autoscaling_policy" "cpu" {
  name                   = "${var.project}-cpu-target"
  autoscaling_group_name = aws_autoscaling_group.app.name
  policy_type            = "TargetTrackingScaling"

  target_tracking_configuration {
    predefined_metric_specification {
      predefined_metric_type = "ASGAverageCPUUtilization"
    }
    target_value = 60.0
  }
}

# Scale on ALB request count per target
resource "aws_autoscaling_policy" "requests" {
  name                   = "${var.project}-request-target"
  autoscaling_group_name = aws_autoscaling_group.app.name
  policy_type            = "TargetTrackingScaling"

  target_tracking_configuration {
    predefined_metric_specification {
      predefined_metric_type = "ALBRequestCountPerTarget"
      resource_label = "${var.alb_arn_suffix}/${var.target_group_arn_suffix}"
    }
    target_value = 1000.0   # 1000 req/target before scaling
  }
}

modules/cloudflare/main.tf — DNS, WAF, Page Rules

# DNS — point domain to ALB (proxied = Cloudflare in front)
resource "cloudflare_record" "root" {
  zone_id = var.zone_id
  name    = var.domain_name
  type    = "CNAME"
  value   = var.alb_dns_name
  proxied = true   # orange-cloud = Cloudflare proxy active
  ttl     = 1      # auto when proxied
}

resource "cloudflare_record" "www" {
  zone_id = var.zone_id
  name    = "www"
  type    = "CNAME"
  value   = var.domain_name
  proxied = true
  ttl     = 1
}

# WAF Rules — block common attacks
resource "cloudflare_ruleset" "waf" {
  zone_id     = var.zone_id
  name        = "WAF Rules"
  description = "Managed WAF + custom rules"
  kind        = "zone"
  phase       = "http_request_firewall_managed"

  rules {
    action      = "execute"
    description = "Cloudflare Managed Ruleset"
    expression  = "true"
    action_parameters {
      id = "efb7b8c949ac4650a09736fc376e9aee"   # Cloudflare Managed Rules
      overrides {
        action            = "block"
        sensitivity_level = "default"
      }
    }
    enabled = true
  }
}

# Custom WAF — rate limiting
resource "cloudflare_ruleset" "rate_limit" {
  zone_id     = var.zone_id
  name        = "Rate Limiting"
  kind        = "zone"
  phase       = "http_ratelimit"

  rules {
    action      = "block"
    description = "Block 100+ req/min per IP on /api"
    expression  = "(http.request.uri.path matches \"^/api\")"
    ratelimit {
      characteristics      = ["cf.colo.id", "ip.src"]
      period               = 60
      requests_per_period  = 100
      mitigation_timeout   = 600
    }
    enabled = true
  }
}

# Security Headers via Transform Rules
resource "cloudflare_ruleset" "security_headers" {
  zone_id     = var.zone_id
  name        = "Security Headers"
  kind        = "zone"
  phase       = "http_response_headers_transform"

  rules {
    action      = "rewrite"
    description = "Add security headers"
    expression  = "true"
    action_parameters {
      headers {
        name      = "Strict-Transport-Security"
        operation = "set"
        value     = "max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains; preload"
      }
      headers {
        name      = "X-Content-Type-Options"
        operation = "set"
        value     = "nosniff"
      }
      headers {
        name      = "X-Frame-Options"
        operation = "set"
        value     = "SAMEORIGIN"
      }
      headers {
        name      = "Permissions-Policy"
        operation = "set"
        value     = "camera=(), microphone=(), geolocation=()"
      }
    }
    enabled = true
  }
}

# Cache rules — cache static assets at edge
resource "cloudflare_ruleset" "cache" {
  zone_id     = var.zone_id
  name        = "Cache Rules"
  kind        = "zone"
  phase       = "http_request_cache_settings"

  rules {
    action      = "set_cache_settings"
    description = "Cache static assets 7 days"
    expression  = "(http.request.uri.path.extension in {\"css\" \"js\" \"png\" \"jpg\" \"webp\" \"woff2\" \"svg\"})"
    action_parameters {
      cache = true
      edge_ttl {
        mode    = "override_origin"
        default = 604800   # 7 days
      }
      browser_ttl {
        mode    = "override_origin"
        default = 86400    # 1 day
      }
    }
    enabled = true
  }

  rules {
    action      = "set_cache_settings"
    description = "Do not cache API responses"
    expression  = "(http.request.uri.path matches \"^/api\")"
    action_parameters {
      cache = false
    }
    enabled = true
  }
}

# Firewall — geo-block (optional example)
resource "cloudflare_ruleset" "firewall_custom" {
  zone_id     = var.zone_id
  name        = "Custom Firewall"
  kind        = "zone"
  phase       = "http_request_firewall_custom"

  rules {
    action      = "challenge"   # CAPTCHA challenge
    description = "Challenge high-risk countries"
    expression  = "(ip.geoip.country in {\"CN\" \"RU\" \"KP\"} and not cf.client.bot)"
    enabled     = false   # set to true if needed
  }
}

# SSL/TLS settings
resource "cloudflare_zone_settings_override" "main" {
  zone_id = var.zone_id
  settings {
    ssl                      = "full_strict"   # end-to-end encryption
    min_tls_version          = "1.2"
    tls_1_3                  = "zrt"           # TLS 1.3 + 0-RTT
    automatic_https_rewrites = "on"
    always_use_https         = "on"
    brotli                   = "on"
    http3                    = "on"
    rocket_loader            = "off"           # may break some JS
    development_mode         = "off"
  }
}
