  --describe --group order-processor-1

Interview Questions — Messaging

What is a Dead Letter Queue and why is it important?
A DLQ is a separate queue where messages are moved after they fail processing N times (maxReceiveCount). It's critical for production systems because: 1) Prevents poison-pill messages (malformed, causes exceptions) from blocking the main queue forever by infinitely retrying. 2) Gives ops team visibility into failures — DLQ messages can be inspected to diagnose bugs. 3) Allows re-processing after a fix — once the bug is fixed, messages can be moved back from DLQ to main queue. 4) Prevents data loss — without DLQ, failed messages eventually expire. Set DLQ retention to 14 days (max for SQS). Alert on DLQ depth > 0.
Explain Kafka partitions and consumer groups.
A Kafka topic is split into partitions — each partition is an ordered, immutable log on a separate broker. Partitioning enables parallelism: multiple consumers can read simultaneously, one per partition. Consumer group: a group of consumers sharing a topic's partitions — each partition assigned to exactly one consumer in the group. Scale consumers by adding instances to the group (up to partition count). If consumers > partitions, extra consumers idle. For ordering: messages with same key always go to same partition. Replication factor: each partition replicated across N brokers — tolerate N-1 broker failures.
🗄️

S. Database DevOps — Migrations, Backup & HA

Intermediate → Advanced

Database Migrations — Flyway

# Flyway migration files — naming: V{version}__{description}.sql
db/migrations/
  V1__create_users_table.sql
  V2__add_email_index.sql
  V3__add_user_roles.sql

# V1__create_users_table.sql
CREATE TABLE users (
    user_id   UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
    name      VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    email     VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

# V2__add_email_index.sql
CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY idx_users_email ON users(email);
-- CONCURRENTLY avoids table lock in PostgreSQL

# Run migrations (in CI/CD pipeline before app deploy)
flyway -url=jdbc:postgresql://localhost:5432/appdb \
       -user=appuser \
       -password=secret \
       -locations=filesystem:./db/migrations \
       migrate

# Check migration status
flyway info

# Validate migrations match applied state
flyway validate

Zero-Downtime Migration Pattern (Expand-Contract)

WRONG (causes downtime): ALTER TABLE users RENAME COLUMN name TO full_name; → Old app breaks immediately reading "name" CORRECT — Expand-Contract in 3 deployments: Deploy 1: ADD COLUMN full_name VARCHAR(255); (backward compatible) Backfill: UPDATE users SET full_name = name; Deploy 2: App reads full_name, writes BOTH name AND full_name Deploy 3: DROP COLUMN name; (old code gone) App reads/writes only full_name

RDS — Production Configuration

# Terraform — RDS PostgreSQL Multi-AZ
resource "aws_db_instance" "main" {
  identifier     = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-db"
  engine         = "postgres"
  engine_version = "16.1"
  instance_class = "db.r6g.xlarge"   # memory-optimized, Graviton

  # Storage
  allocated_storage     = 100
  max_allocated_storage = 1000        # auto-scaling storage up to 1TB
  storage_type          = "gp3"
  storage_encrypted     = true
  kms_key_id            = aws_kms_key.rds.arn

  # Credentials
  db_name  = var.db_name
  username = var.db_username
  manage_master_user_password = true  # AWS manages in Secrets Manager

  # High Availability
  multi_az = true                     # synchronous standby in another AZ

  # Backups
  backup_retention_period   = 30      # 30 days PITR
  backup_window             = "03:00-04:00"
  maintenance_window        = "sun:05:00-sun:06:00"
  copy_tags_to_snapshot     = true
  delete_automated_backups  = false

  # Performance
  performance_insights_enabled = true
  performance_insights_retention_period = 7
  monitoring_interval = 60           # Enhanced Monitoring every 60s
  monitoring_role_arn = aws_iam_role.rds_monitoring.arn
  enabled_cloudwatch_logs_exports = ["postgresql", "upgrade"]

  # Security
  publicly_accessible    = false
  db_subnet_group_name   = aws_db_subnet_group.main.name
  vpc_security_group_ids = [aws_security_group.rds.id]
  deletion_protection    = true

  # Upgrade
  allow_major_version_upgrade = false
  auto_minor_version_upgrade  = true

  final_snapshot_identifier = "${var.project}-final-${formatdate("YYYY-MM-DD", timestamp())}"
}

# Read Replica (for reporting / read-heavy workloads)
resource "aws_db_instance" "replica" {
  identifier             = "${var.project}-${var.environment}-replica"
  replicate_source_db    = aws_db_instance.main.identifier
  instance_class         = "db.r6g.large"
  publicly_accessible    = false
  vpc_security_group_ids = [aws_security_group.rds.id]
  skip_final_snapshot    = true
  storage_encrypted      = true
}

Backup & Recovery

# Manual snapshot before major change
aws rds create-db-snapshot \
  --db-instance-identifier myapp-prod-db \
  --db-snapshot-identifier pre-migration-$(date +%Y%m%d-%H%M)

# Point-in-Time Recovery (restore to any second in retention window)
aws rds restore-db-instance-to-point-in-time \
  --source-db-instance-identifier myapp-prod-db \
  --target-db-instance-identifier myapp-restored \
  --restore-time "2024-01-15T02:30:00Z"

# PostgreSQL — manual backup to S3
pg_dump -h $DB_HOST -U $DB_USER -d $DB_NAME \
  --format=custom --compress=9 \
  -f /tmp/backup-$(date +%Y%m%d).dump

aws s3 cp /tmp/backup-$(date +%Y%m%d).dump \
  s3://my-backups/db/postgres/

# Restore
pg_restore -h $DB_HOST -U $DB_USER -d $DB_NAME \
  --clean --if-exists /tmp/backup.dump

Interview Questions — Database DevOps

How do you run database migrations in a CI/CD pipeline without downtime?
Use the expand-contract pattern: 1) Never rename or drop columns in the same deploy as the code that uses the new schema. 2) Phase 1 (migration): add new nullable column, create new table — backward compatible with current code. 3) Phase 2 (backfill): populate new column for existing rows via background job. 4) Phase 3 (code deploy): release new app version that reads from new column. 5) Phase 4 (cleanup): drop old column in a later deploy after confirming no old code uses it. In CI: run flyway migrate as a step before deploying new app containers. Use transactions in migrations. Never run DDL in application startup code.
🌐

T. Advanced Nginx Configuration

Intermediate → Advanced

Production Nginx Configuration

# /etc/nginx/nginx.conf — production hardened
user nginx;
worker_processes auto;                    # one per CPU core
worker_rlimit_nofile 65535;
error_log /var/log/nginx/error.log warn;
pid /run/nginx.pid;

events {
    worker_connections 4096;              # per worker
    use epoll;                            # Linux best I/O model
    multi_accept on;
}

http {
    include       /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type  application/octet-stream;

    # Logging
    log_format main '$remote_addr - $remote_user [$time_local] "$request" '
                    '$status $body_bytes_sent "$http_referer" '
                    '"$http_user_agent" "$http_x_forwarded_for" '
                    'rt=$request_time urt=$upstream_response_time';
    access_log /var/log/nginx/access.log main buffer=16k flush=2s;

    # Performance
    sendfile        on;
    tcp_nopush      on;
    tcp_nodelay     on;
    keepalive_timeout 65;
    keepalive_requests 1000;

    # Gzip
    gzip on;
    gzip_vary on;
    gzip_proxied any;
    gzip_comp_level 6;
    gzip_min_length 1024;
    gzip_types text/plain text/css text/xml text/javascript
               application/json application/javascript application/xml+rss
               image/svg+xml;

    # Security
    server_tokens off;                    # hide Nginx version
    more_clear_headers Server;            # requires headers-more module

    # Rate limiting
    limit_req_zone $binary_remote_addr zone=api:10m rate=100r/m;
    limit_req_zone $binary_remote_addr zone=login:10m rate=5r/m;
    limit_conn_zone $binary_remote_addr zone=addr:10m;

    # Upstream — app servers (load balancing)
    upstream app_backend {
        least_conn;                       # least connections LB
        keepalive 32;                     # keep 32 persistent connections

        server 10.0.11.10:3000 weight=1 max_fails=3 fail_timeout=30s;
        server 10.0.12.10:3000 weight=1 max_fails=3 fail_timeout=30s;
        server 10.0.11.11:3000 backup;   # only if primaries fail
    }

    include /etc/nginx/conf.d/*.conf;
}

# /etc/nginx/conf.d/app.conf
server {
    listen 80;
    server_name myapp.com www.myapp.com;
    return 301 https://$host$request_uri;   # redirect all HTTP → HTTPS
}

server {
    listen 443 ssl http2;
    server_name myapp.com www.myapp.com;

    # SSL
    ssl_certificate     /etc/nginx/certs/fullchain.pem;
    ssl_certificate_key /etc/nginx/certs/privkey.pem;
    ssl_session_cache   shared:SSL:10m;
    ssl_session_timeout 1d;
    ssl_protocols       TLSv1.2 TLSv1.3;
    ssl_ciphers         ECDHE-ECDSA-AES128-GCM-SHA256:ECDHE-RSA-AES128-GCM-SHA256:ECDHE-ECDSA-AES256-GCM-SHA384;
    ssl_prefer_server_ciphers off;
    ssl_stapling on;
    ssl_stapling_verify on;

    # Security headers
    add_header Strict-Transport-Security "max-age=63072000; includeSubDomains; preload" always;
    add_header X-Frame-Options "SAMEORIGIN" always;
    add_header X-Content-Type-Options "nosniff" always;
    add_header Referrer-Policy "strict-origin-when-cross-origin" always;
    add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; script-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline'; style-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline';" always;

    # Root / static files
    root /var/www/html;
    index index.html;

    # Static files — cache at browser
    location ~* \.(js|css|png|jpg|jpeg|gif|ico|svg|woff2|webp)$ {
        expires 1y;
        add_header Cache-Control "public, immutable";
        access_log off;
    }

    # API — proxy to backend, rate limited
    location /api/ {
        limit_req zone=api burst=20 nodelay;
        limit_conn addr 10;

        proxy_pass http://app_backend;
        proxy_http_version 1.1;
        proxy_set_header Upgrade $http_upgrade;
        proxy_set_header Connection "upgrade";   # for WebSockets
        proxy_set_header Host $host;
        proxy_set_header X-Real-IP $remote_addr;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-For $proxy_add_x_forwarded_for;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-Proto $scheme;

        proxy_connect_timeout 5s;
        proxy_send_timeout    60s;
        proxy_read_timeout    60s;
        proxy_buffering       on;
        proxy_buffer_size     4k;
        proxy_buffers         8 4k;

        # Upstream health — if backend returns 502/503/504, try next
        proxy_next_upstream error timeout http_502 http_503 http_504;
        proxy_next_upstream_tries 2;
    }

    # Login endpoint — strict rate limit
    location /api/auth/login {
        limit_req zone=login burst=3 nodelay;
        proxy_pass http://app_backend;
    }

    # Health check — no logging, no rate limit
    location /health {
        access_log off;
        proxy_pass http://app_backend;
    }

    # SPA fallback — all non-file routes → index.html
    location / {
        try_files $uri $uri/ /index.html;
    }
}

Interview Questions — Nginx

Nginx returns 502 Bad Gateway. How do you diagnose?
502 = Nginx received an invalid response from the upstream backend. Debug steps: 1) Check Nginx error log: tail -50 /var/log/nginx/error.log — look for "connect() failed" or "upstream timed out". 2) Verify backend is running: curl -v http://localhost:3000/health directly on app server. 3) Check upstream config in nginx.conf — correct IP:port? 4) Check backend logs for crash. 5) Check proxy_read_timeout — if app is slow to respond, increase it. 6) Check file descriptor limits: ulimit -n — if too low, Nginx can't open connections. 7) If all backends down: check ASG health, check DB connectivity from app.
🐍

U. Python & Scripting for DevOps

Intermediate

boto3 — AWS SDK for Python

import boto3
import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta, timezone

# AWS clients
ec2     = boto3.client('ec2', region_name='us-east-1')
s3      = boto3.client('s3')
ssm     = boto3.client('ssm')
secrets = boto3.client('secretsmanager')
ecs     = boto3.client('ecs')

# ── EC2: Find and stop idle instances ────────────────────────────────────────
def stop_idle_instances(cpu_threshold=5.0, hours=24):
    """Stop EC2 instances with avg CPU < threshold for the past N hours."""
    cw = boto3.client('cloudwatch')

    instances = ec2.describe_instances(
        Filters=[{'Name': 'instance-state-name', 'Values': ['running']},
                 {'Name': 'tag:Environment',      'Values': ['dev']}]
    )

    to_stop = []
    for reservation in instances['Reservations']:
        for inst in reservation['Instances']:
            iid = inst['InstanceId']
            metrics = cw.get_metric_statistics(
                Namespace   = 'AWS/EC2',
                MetricName  = 'CPUUtilization',
                Dimensions  = [{'Name': 'InstanceId', 'Value': iid}],
                StartTime   = datetime.now(timezone.utc) - timedelta(hours=hours),
                EndTime     = datetime.now(timezone.utc),
                Period      = 3600,
                Statistics  = ['Average']
            )
            if metrics['Datapoints']:
                avg_cpu = sum(p['Average'] for p in metrics['Datapoints']) / len(metrics['Datapoints'])
                if avg_cpu < cpu_threshold:
                    to_stop.append(iid)
                    print(f"  {iid}: avg CPU {avg_cpu:.1f}% → stopping")

    if to_stop:
        ec2.stop_instances(InstanceIds=to_stop)
        print(f"Stopped {len(to_stop)} idle instances")

# ── S3: Clean old backups ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────
def cleanup_old_backups(bucket, prefix, days_to_keep=30):
    """Delete S3 objects older than N days."""
    paginator = s3.get_paginator('list_objects_v2')
    cutoff = datetime.now(timezone.utc) - timedelta(days=days_to_keep)
    deleted = 0

    for page in paginator.paginate(Bucket=bucket, Prefix=prefix):
        for obj in page.get('Contents', []):
            if obj['LastModified'] < cutoff:
                s3.delete_object(Bucket=bucket, Key=obj['Key'])
                deleted += 1

    print(f"Deleted {deleted} objects from s3://{bucket}/{prefix}")

# ── Secrets Manager: rotate a secret ─────────────────────────────────────────
def get_secret(secret_name):
    response = secrets.get_secret_value(SecretId=secret_name)
    if 'SecretString' in response:
        return json.loads(response['SecretString'])
    return response['SecretBinary']

# ── ECS: force new deployment ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
def force_ecs_deploy(cluster, service):
    """Force ECS service to pull latest image and redeploy."""
    response = ecs.update_service(
        cluster             = cluster,
        service             = service,
        forceNewDeployment  = True
    )
    print(f"Forced deployment: {response['service']['serviceName']}")
    print(f"  Status: {response['service']['status']}")
    print(f"  Running: {response['service']['runningCount']}")
    print(f"  Desired: {response['service']['desiredCount']}")

# ── SSM Parameter Store ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────
def get_param(name, decrypt=True):
    return ssm.get_parameter(Name=name, WithDecryption=decrypt)['Parameter']['Value']

def put_param(name, value, param_type='SecureString'):
    ssm.put_parameter(Name=name, Value=value, Type=param_type, Overwrite=True)

if __name__ == '__main__':
    stop_idle_instances(cpu_threshold=5.0, hours=24)
    cleanup_old_backups('my-backups', 'db/postgres/', days_to_keep=30)

Python: Health Check Monitor Script

import requests, smtplib, time, logging
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import List

logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO, format='%(asctime)s %(levelname)s %(message)s')

@dataclass
class Endpoint:
    name: str
    url: str
    expected_status: int = 200
    timeout: int = 10

ENDPOINTS = [
    Endpoint("API",      "https://api.myapp.com/health"),
    Endpoint("Frontend", "https://myapp.com"),
    Endpoint("Admin",    "https://admin.myapp.com/health"),
]

def check_endpoint(ep: Endpoint) -> dict:
    try:
        r = requests.get(ep.url, timeout=ep.timeout)
        ok = r.status_code == ep.expected_status
        return {"name": ep.name, "ok": ok, "status": r.status_code,
                "latency_ms": round(r.elapsed.total_seconds() * 1000)}
    except Exception as e:
        return {"name": ep.name, "ok": False, "error": str(e)}

def send_alert(results: List[dict]):
    failed = [r for r in results if not r['ok']]
    if not failed:
        return
    body = "\n".join(f"❌ {r['name']}: {r.get('error', f'HTTP {r[\"status\"]}')}" for r in failed)
    msg = MIMEText(body)
    msg['Subject'] = f"ALERT: {len(failed)} endpoint(s) down"
    msg['From'] = "monitor@myapp.com"
    msg['To']   = "oncall@myapp.com"
    with smtplib.SMTP('smtp.gmail.com', 587) as s:
        s.starttls()
        s.login("monitor@myapp.com", "app_password")
        s.sendmail(msg['From'], [msg['To']], msg.as_string())
    logging.warning("Alert sent: %s", body)

def monitor():
    while True:
        results = [check_endpoint(ep) for ep in ENDPOINTS]
        for r in results:
            status = "✅" if r['ok'] else "❌"
            logging.info("%s %s %s", status, r['name'], r.get('latency_ms', r.get('error', '')))
        send_alert(results)
        time.sleep(60)

if __name__ == '__main__':
    monitor()

Interview Questions — Python for DevOps

Write a Python script to find EC2 instances not tagged with Environment and list them.
import boto3
ec2 = boto3.client('ec2', region_name='us-east-1')
response = ec2.describe_instances(
    Filters=[{'Name': 'instance-state-name', 'Values': ['running']}]
)
untagged = []
for r in response['Reservations']:
    for inst in r['Instances']:
        tags = {t['Key']: t['Value'] for t in inst.get('Tags', [])}
        if 'Environment' not in tags:
            untagged.append(inst['InstanceId'])
print(f"Untagged instances ({len(untagged)}): {untagged}")
This demonstrates boto3 pagination awareness (add paginator for >100 instances), filtering, and tag inspection — common interview pattern.

V. OpenTelemetry — Modern Observability

Advanced
OpenTelemetry (OTel) is the CNCF standard for collecting metrics, logs, and traces — vendor-neutral. Instrument once, send to any backend (Jaeger, Grafana Tempo, Datadog, AWS X-Ray).

OTel Architecture

Your App (instrumented with OTel SDK) │ traces/metrics/logs (OTLP protocol) ▼ OTel Collector (sidecar or daemonset in K8s) │ receives, processes, batches ├─► Jaeger / Grafana Tempo (traces) ├─► Prometheus (metrics via OTLP receiver) └─► Elasticsearch / Loki (logs)

Instrument a Node.js App

// tracing.js — must be loaded first (--require ./tracing.js)
const { NodeSDK } = require('@opentelemetry/sdk-node');
const { getNodeAutoInstrumentations } = require('@opentelemetry/auto-instrumentations-node');
const { OTLPTraceExporter } = require('@opentelemetry/exporter-trace-otlp-grpc');
const { OTLPMetricExporter } = require('@opentelemetry/exporter-metrics-otlp-grpc');
const { PeriodicExportingMetricReader } = require('@opentelemetry/sdk-metrics');
const { Resource } = require('@opentelemetry/resources');
const { SEMRESATTRS_SERVICE_NAME, SEMRESATTRS_SERVICE_VERSION } = require('@opentelemetry/semantic-conventions');

const sdk = new NodeSDK({
  resource: new Resource({
    [SEMRESATTRS_SERVICE_NAME]:    'api-service',
    [SEMRESATTRS_SERVICE_VERSION]: process.env.APP_VERSION || '1.0.0',
    environment: process.env.NODE_ENV,
  }),
  traceExporter: new OTLPTraceExporter({
    url: process.env.OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT || 'http://otel-collector:4317',
  }),
  metricReader: new PeriodicExportingMetricReader({
    exporter: new OTLPMetricExporter({
      url: process.env.OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT || 'http://otel-collector:4317',
    }),
    exportIntervalMillis: 15000,
  }),
  instrumentations: [
    getNodeAutoInstrumentations({
      '@opentelemetry/instrumentation-http':     { enabled: true },
      '@opentelemetry/instrumentation-express':  { enabled: true },
      '@opentelemetry/instrumentation-pg':       { enabled: true },
      '@opentelemetry/instrumentation-redis':    { enabled: true },
    }),
  ],
});
sdk.start();

OTel Collector — K8s DaemonSet

# otel-collector-config.yaml
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: otel-collector-config
  namespace: monitoring
data:
  config.yaml: |
    receivers:
      otlp:
        protocols:
          grpc:
            endpoint: 0.0.0.0:4317
          http:
            endpoint: 0.0.0.0:4318
      prometheus:
        config:
          scrape_configs:
          - job_name: 'k8s-pods'
            kubernetes_sd_configs:
            - role: pod

    processors:
      batch:
        timeout: 5s
        send_batch_size: 512
      resource:
        attributes:
        - action: insert
          key: k8s.cluster.name
          value: myapp-prod
      memory_limiter:
        limit_mib: 256

    exporters:
      otlp/jaeger:
        endpoint: jaeger-collector:4317
        tls:
          insecure: true
      prometheusremotewrite:
        endpoint: http://prometheus:9090/api/v1/write
      logging:
        loglevel: warn

    service:
      pipelines:
        traces:
          receivers:  [otlp]
          processors: [memory_limiter, batch, resource]
          exporters:  [otlp/jaeger]
        metrics:
          receivers:  [otlp, prometheus]
          processors: [memory_limiter, batch]
          exporters:  [prometheusremotewrite]

Interview Questions — OpenTelemetry

What is a trace and a span in distributed tracing?
A trace represents the complete journey of a request through your distributed system — from the initial HTTP request to the final response, across all microservices. A span is one unit of work within a trace — e.g., "API received request", "DB query executed", "cache lookup". Spans have: start time, duration, status (ok/error), attributes (HTTP method, URL, status code), and events (log-like entries). Spans link to each other via parent-child relationships — this creates the trace "tree". A trace ID is propagated via HTTP headers (W3C TraceContext: traceparent) between services, allowing you to reconstruct the full request path.

Terraform Cheat Sheet

Terraform Workflow
terraform init → terraform plan → terraform apply → terraform destroy
State: local (terraform.tfstate) | Remote (S3 + DynamoDB lock) | Terraform Cloud

Core Commands

# Initialization
terraform init                        # Download providers & modules
terraform init -upgrade               # Upgrade providers
terraform init -backend-config=prod.tfbackend

# Planning & Applying
terraform plan -out=tfplan            # Save plan
terraform apply tfplan                # Apply saved plan
terraform apply -auto-approve         # Skip confirmation
terraform apply -target=module.vpc    # Target specific resource
terraform apply -var="env=prod"       # Pass variable

# State management
terraform state list                  # List resources in state
terraform state show aws_instance.web # Show resource details
terraform state mv aws_instance.old aws_instance.new
terraform state rm aws_instance.temp  # Remove from state (NOT destroy)
terraform import aws_s3_bucket.my-bucket my-bucket-name

# Workspace management
terraform workspace new staging
terraform workspace select prod
terraform workspace list
terraform workspace delete staging

# Debugging
terraform fmt -recursive              # Format all .tf files
terraform validate                    # Validate config
terraform console                     # Interactive console
TF_LOG=DEBUG terraform apply          # Debug logging
terraform show tfplan                 # Show plan file human-readable
terraform graph | dot -Tsvg > graph.svg  # Dependency graph

# Destroy
terraform destroy -target=module.rds  # Destroy specific
terraform destroy -auto-approve

# variables.tf
variable "environment" {
  type        = string
  description = "Deployment environment"
  default     = "dev"
  validation {
    condition     = contains(["dev", "staging", "prod"], var.environment)
    error_message = "Must be dev, staging, or prod."
  }
}

variable "instance_count" {
  type    = number
  default = 2
}

variable "tags" {
  type    = map(string)
  default = {}
}

variable "allowed_cidrs" {
  type    = list(string)
  default = ["10.0.0.0/8"]
}

# outputs.tf
output "alb_dns" {
  value       = aws_lb.main.dns_name
  description = "ALB DNS name"
}

output "db_endpoint" {
  value     = aws_db_instance.main.endpoint
  sensitive = true
}

# locals.tf
locals {
  name_prefix  = "${var.project}-${var.environment}"
  common_tags  = merge(var.tags, {
    Project     = var.project
    Environment = var.environment
    ManagedBy   = "Terraform"
  })
  is_prod = var.environment == "prod"
  az_count = local.is_prod ? 3 : 2
}

Data Sources & Dynamic Blocks

# Data sources
data "aws_ami" "amazon_linux" {
  most_recent = true
  owners      = ["amazon"]
  filter {
    name   = "name"
    values = ["amzn2-ami-hvm-*-x86_64-gp2"]
  }
}

data "aws_availability_zones" "available" {
  state = "available"
}

data "aws_caller_identity" "current" {}
data "aws_region" "current" {}

# Use: data.aws_region.current.name

# Dynamic blocks
resource "aws_security_group" "web" {
  name   = "web-sg"
  vpc_id = aws_vpc.main.id

  dynamic "ingress" {
    for_each = var.ingress_rules
    content {
      from_port   = ingress.value.port
      to_port     = ingress.value.port
      protocol    = ingress.value.protocol
      cidr_blocks = ingress.value.cidrs
    }
  }
}

# for_each with maps
resource "aws_subnet" "private" {
  for_each = {
    for idx, az in data.aws_availability_zones.available.names :
    az => {
      az   = az
      cidr = cidrsubnet(var.vpc_cidr, 8, idx + 10)
    }
  }
  vpc_id            = aws_vpc.main.id
  availability_zone = each.value.az
  cidr_block        = each.value.cidr
}

# count
resource "aws_instance" "web" {
  count         = var.instance_count
  ami           = data.aws_ami.amazon_linux.id
  instance_type = var.instance_type
  tags = {
    Name = "${local.name_prefix}-web-${count.index + 1}"
  }
}

Terraform Backend & Remote State

# backend.tf
terraform {
  required_version = ">= 1.5"
  required_providers {
    aws = {
      source  = "hashicorp/aws"
      version = "~> 5.0"
    }
  }
  backend "s3" {
    bucket         = "my-tfstate-bucket"
    key            = "prod/terraform.tfstate"
    region         = "us-east-1"
    encrypt        = true
    dynamodb_table = "terraform-lock"
  }
}

# Read another module's outputs
data "terraform_remote_state" "vpc" {
  backend = "s3"
  config = {
    bucket = "my-tfstate-bucket"
    key    = "prod/vpc/terraform.tfstate"
    region = "us-east-1"
  }
}

# Use: data.terraform_remote_state.vpc.outputs.vpc_id

# Atlantis workflow (PR-based Terraform)
# atlantis.yaml
version: 3
projects:
  - name: prod-vpc
    dir: environments/prod/vpc
    workspace: default
    autoplan:
      when_modified: ["*.tf", "../../../modules/**/*.tf"]
    apply_requirements: [approved, mergeable]
Q: How do you handle Terraform state locking and what happens if a lock gets stuck?
A: Terraform uses DynamoDB for state locking — when terraform apply runs, it writes a lock record to DynamoDB preventing concurrent modifications. If a lock gets stuck (e.g., interrupted apply), use terraform force-unlock <LOCK_ID> — the lock ID is shown in the error message. To prevent stuck locks, use CI/CD with proper cleanup and set DynamoDB TTL on lock items.

        url: http://localhost/health
        status_code: 200

Roles & Handlers

# roles/nginx/tasks/main.yml
---
- name: Install nginx
  package:
    name: nginx
    state: present

- name: Deploy nginx config
  template:
    src: nginx.conf.j2
    dest: /etc/nginx/nginx.conf
    owner: root
    group: root
    mode: '0644'
    validate: 'nginx -t -c %s'
  notify: Reload nginx

- name: Deploy site config
  template:
    src: site.conf.j2
    dest: /etc/nginx/conf.d/site.conf
  notify: Reload nginx

- name: Enable and start nginx
  service:
    name: nginx
    state: started
    enabled: yes

# roles/nginx/handlers/main.yml
---
- name: Reload nginx
  service:
    name: nginx
    state: reloaded

- name: Restart nginx
  service:
    name: nginx
    state: restarted

# roles/nginx/templates/nginx.conf.j2
worker_processes {{ ansible_processor_vcpus }};
events { worker_connections 1024; }
http {
  server_name {{ inventory_hostname }};
  root {{ app_root_dir }};
}

Loops, Conditionals & Error Handling

---
- name: Advanced task examples
  hosts: all
  vars:
    packages:
      - { name: git, state: present }
      - { name: curl, state: present }
      - { name: vim, state: latest }
  tasks:
    # Loop
    - name: Install packages
      package:
        name: "{{ item.name }}"
        state: "{{ item.state }}"
      loop: "{{ packages }}"

    # Conditional
    - name: Start firewalld (RHEL only)
      service:
        name: firewalld
        state: started
      when: ansible_os_family == "RedHat"

    # Register & use result
    - name: Check if app is running
      command: systemctl is-active myapp
      register: app_status
      changed_when: false
      failed_when: false

    - name: Start app if not running
      service:
        name: myapp
        state: started
      when: app_status.rc != 0

    # Error handling
    - name: Risky task
      command: /opt/deploy.sh
      ignore_errors: yes
      register: deploy_result

    - name: Rollback on failure
      command: /opt/rollback.sh
      when: deploy_result.failed

    # Block / rescue / always
    - block:
        - name: Deploy app
          command: /opt/deploy.sh
        - name: Run smoke tests
          uri:
            url: http://localhost/health
      rescue:
        - name: Rollback
          command: /opt/rollback.sh
        - name: Notify on failure
          slack:
            token: "{{ slack_token }}"
            msg: "Deploy failed on {{ inventory_hostname }}"
      always:
        - name: Send deploy event
          command: /opt/send-event.sh
Q: What is the difference between `include_tasks` and `import_tasks`?
A: import_tasks is static — files are parsed at playbook load time, so variables in the filename must be known beforehand; tasks show up in --list-tasks. include_tasks is dynamic — evaluated at runtime, supports dynamic filenames (e.g., {{ ansible_os_family }}.yml), can be used inside loops. Use import_* for static structure and include_* for dynamic, conditional, or looped inclusion.

Helm Cheat Sheet

Helm Concepts
Chart (package) → Release (deployed instance) → Repository (chart registry)
values.yaml → templates/*.yaml → Kubernetes manifests

Core Commands

# Repo management
helm repo add stable https://charts.helm.sh/stable
helm repo add bitnami https://charts.bitnami.com/bitnami
helm repo update
helm repo list
helm search repo nginx
helm search hub wordpress           # Search Artifact Hub

# Install / Upgrade / Rollback
helm install my-nginx bitnami/nginx -n web --create-namespace
helm install my-app ./mychart -f values-prod.yaml
helm install my-app ./mychart --set image.tag=v1.2.0
helm upgrade my-app ./mychart -f values-prod.yaml --install  # install if not exists
helm upgrade my-app ./mychart --set image.tag=v2.0.0 --atomic  # rollback on failure
helm rollback my-app 1              # Rollback to revision 1
helm uninstall my-app -n web

# Inspection
helm list -A                        # All namespaces
helm status my-app
helm history my-app                 # Release history
helm get values my-app              # User-supplied values
helm get values my-app --all        # All values (merged)
helm get manifest my-app            # Rendered manifests

# Development
helm create mychart                 # Scaffold new chart
helm lint mychart/                  # Validate chart
helm template my-app ./mychart -f values.yaml  # Render locally
helm template my-app ./mychart | kubectl apply --dry-run=client -f -
helm package mychart/               # Package to .tgz
helm dependency update mychart/     # Fetch dependencies

# Plugin
helm plugin install https://github.com/databus23/helm-diff
helm diff upgrade my-app ./mychart -f values-prod.yaml

Chart Structure & Templates

# Chart.yaml
apiVersion: v2
name: myapp
description: My Application
type: application

  - name: postgresql
    version: "12.x.x"
    repository: https://charts.bitnami.com/bitnami
    condition: postgresql.enabled

replicaCount: 2

  repository: myapp
  tag: "1.0.0"
  pullPolicy: IfNotPresent
service:
  type: ClusterIP
  port: 80
ingress:
  enabled: false
  host: myapp.example.com
resources:
  requests:
    cpu: 100m
    memory: 128Mi
  limits:
    cpu: 500m
    memory: 512Mi
postgresql:
  enabled: true
  auth:
    database: myapp
    username: myapp

# templates/deployment.yaml
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: {{ include "myapp.fullname" . }}
  labels:
    {{- include "myapp.labels" . | nindent 4 }}
spec:
  replicas: {{ .Values.replicaCount }}
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      {{- include "myapp.selectorLabels" . | nindent 6 }}
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        {{- include "myapp.selectorLabels" . | nindent 8 }}
    spec:
      containers:
        - name: {{ .Chart.Name }}
          image: "{{ .Values.image.repository }}:{{ .Values.image.tag | default .Chart.AppVersion }}"
          ports:
            - containerPort: 80
          env:
            - name: DB_HOST
              value: {{ include "myapp.fullname" . }}-postgresql
            - name: DB_PASSWORD
              valueFrom:
                secretKeyRef:
                  name: {{ include "myapp.fullname" . }}-secret
                  key: db-password
          resources:
            {{- toYaml .Values.resources | nindent 12 }}
          {{- if .Values.probes.enabled }}
          livenessProbe:
            httpGet:
              path: /healthz
              port: 80
            initialDelaySeconds: 30
          {{- end }}

# templates/_helpers.tpl
{{- define "myapp.fullname" -}}
{{- printf "%s-%s" .Release.Name .Chart.Name | trunc 63 | trimSuffix "-" }}
{{- end }}

{{- define "myapp.labels" -}}
helm.sh/chart: {{ .Chart.Name }}-{{ .Chart.Version }}
app.kubernetes.io/name: {{ .Chart.Name }}
app.kubernetes.io/instance: {{ .Release.Name }}
app.kubernetes.io/managed-by: {{ .Release.Service }}
{{- end }}
Q: What is the difference between `helm upgrade --install` and `helm install`, and when would you use `--atomic`?
A: helm upgrade --install installs if the release doesn't exist, upgrades otherwise — ideal for CI/CD pipelines where you don't know the state. --atomic sets a timeout and automatically rolls back to the previous release if the upgrade fails (pods don't become Ready), ensuring you never leave a release in a broken state. Always use --atomic in production deployments.

Project 8: Serverless REST API — Lambda + API Gateway + DynamoDB + Terraform

Architecture
Client → API Gateway (HTTP API) → Lambda (Go/Node.js) → DynamoDB
→ CloudWatch Logs | X-Ray Tracing | Secrets Manager
Terraform manages all resources | GitHub Actions CI/CD

Project Overview

Production-ready serverless REST API with authentication, tracing, and zero-downtime deployments. Handles 10k+ req/sec at ~$0.0000002 per request.

Lambda Handler (Node.js)

// src/handlers/users.js
const { DynamoDBClient } = require("@aws-sdk/client-dynamodb");
const { DynamoDBDocumentClient, GetCommand, PutCommand, QueryCommand, DeleteCommand } = require("@aws-sdk/lib-dynamodb");
const { randomUUID } = require("crypto");

const client = new DynamoDBClient({ region: process.env.AWS_REGION });
const ddb = DynamoDBDocumentClient.from(client);
const TABLE = process.env.USERS_TABLE;

exports.handler = async (event) => {
  const { httpMethod, pathParameters, body } = event;
  const userId = pathParameters?.id;

  try {
    switch (httpMethod) {
      case "GET":
        if (userId) return getUser(userId);
        return listUsers();
      case "POST":
        return createUser(JSON.parse(body));
      case "PUT":
        return updateUser(userId, JSON.parse(body));
      case "DELETE":
        return deleteUser(userId);
      default:
        return response(405, { error: "Method not allowed" });
    }
  } catch (err) {
    console.error("Error:", JSON.stringify(err));
    return response(500, { error: "Internal server error" });
  }
};

const getUser = async (id) => {
  const { Item } = await ddb.send(new GetCommand({
    TableName: TABLE,
    Key: { PK: `USER#${id}`, SK: "PROFILE" }
  }));
  return Item
    ? response(200, Item)
    : response(404, { error: "User not found" });
};

const createUser = async (data) => {
  const id = randomUUID();
  const now = new Date().toISOString();
  const item = {
    PK: `USER#${id}`,
    SK: "PROFILE",
    id,
    email: data.email,
    name: data.name,
    createdAt: now,
    updatedAt: now,
    GSI1PK: `EMAIL#${data.email}`,
    GSI1SK: now,
  };
  await ddb.send(new PutCommand({
    TableName: TABLE,
    Item: item,
    ConditionExpression: "attribute_not_exists(PK)",
  }));
  return response(201, item);
};

const response = (statusCode, body) => ({
  statusCode,
  headers: {
    "Content-Type": "application/json",
    "Access-Control-Allow-Origin": "*",
  },
  body: JSON.stringify(body),
});

Terraform — Complete Infrastructure

# main.tf
terraform {
  required_providers {
    aws = { source = "hashicorp/aws", version = "~> 5.0" }
    archive = { source = "hashicorp/archive", version = "~> 2.0" }
  }
  backend "s3" {
    bucket         = "my-tfstate"
    key            = "serverless-api/terraform.tfstate"
    region         = "us-east-1"
    dynamodb_table = "terraform-lock"
    encrypt        = true
  }
}

# DynamoDB Table
resource "aws_dynamodb_table" "users" {
  name           = "${var.app_name}-users-${var.env}"
  billing_mode   = "PAY_PER_REQUEST"
  hash_key       = "PK"
  range_key      = "SK"

  attribute { name = "PK";    type = "S" }
  attribute { name = "SK";    type = "S" }
  attribute { name = "GSI1PK"; type = "S" }
  attribute { name = "GSI1SK"; type = "S" }

  global_secondary_index {
    name            = "GSI1"
    hash_key        = "GSI1PK"
    range_key       = "GSI1SK"
    projection_type = "ALL"
  }

  point_in_time_recovery { enabled = true }
  server_side_encryption  { enabled = true }

  tags = local.common_tags
}

# Lambda package
data "archive_file" "lambda" {
  type        = "zip"
  source_dir  = "${path.module}/../src"
  output_path = "${path.module}/dist/lambda.zip"
}

# IAM Role
resource "aws_iam_role" "lambda" {
  name = "${var.app_name}-lambda-role"
  assume_role_policy = jsonencode({
    Version = "2012-10-17"
    Statement = [{ Effect = "Allow", Principal = { Service = "lambda.amazonaws.com" }, Action = "sts:AssumeRole" }]
  })
}

resource "aws_iam_role_policy" "lambda" {
  role = aws_iam_role.lambda.id
  policy = jsonencode({
    Version = "2012-10-17"
    Statement = [
      {
        Effect   = "Allow"
        Action   = ["dynamodb:GetItem","dynamodb:PutItem","dynamodb:UpdateItem","dynamodb:DeleteItem","dynamodb:Query","dynamodb:Scan"]
        Resource = [aws_dynamodb_table.users.arn, "${aws_dynamodb_table.users.arn}/index/*"]
      },
      {
        Effect   = "Allow"
        Action   = ["logs:CreateLogGroup","logs:CreateLogStream","logs:PutLogEvents","xray:PutTraceSegments","xray:PutTelemetryRecords"]
        Resource = "*"
      }
    ]
  })
}

# Lambda Function
resource "aws_lambda_function" "api" {
  function_name    = "${var.app_name}-api-${var.env}"
  filename         = data.archive_file.lambda.output_path
  source_code_hash = data.archive_file.lambda.output_base64sha256
  handler          = "handlers/users.handler"
  runtime          = "nodejs20.x"
  role             = aws_iam_role.lambda.arn
  timeout          = 30
  memory_size      = 512

  environment {
    variables = {
      USERS_TABLE = aws_dynamodb_table.users.name
      ENV         = var.env
    }
  }

  tracing_config { mode = "Active" }  # X-Ray

  # Provisioned concurrency for prod
  dynamic "provisioned_concurrency_config" {
    for_each = var.env == "prod" ? [1] : []
    content {
      provisioned_concurrent_executions = 5
    }
  }

  tags = local.common_tags
}

# Lambda alias + versioning
resource "aws_lambda_alias" "live" {
  name             = "live"
  function_name    = aws_lambda_function.api.function_name
  function_version = aws_lambda_function.api.version
}

# API Gateway HTTP API
resource "aws_apigatewayv2_api" "main" {
  name          = "${var.app_name}-api"
  protocol_type = "HTTP"
  cors_configuration {
    allow_origins = ["*"]
    allow_methods = ["GET","POST","PUT","DELETE","OPTIONS"]
    allow_headers = ["Content-Type","Authorization"]
    max_age       = 300
  }
}

resource "aws_apigatewayv2_integration" "lambda" {
  api_id                 = aws_apigatewayv2_api.main.id
  integration_type       = "AWS_PROXY"
  integration_uri        = aws_lambda_alias.live.invoke_arn
  payload_format_version = "2.0"
}

resource "aws_apigatewayv2_route" "users_list" {
  api_id    = aws_apigatewayv2_api.main.id
  route_key = "GET /users"
  target    = "integrations/${aws_apigatewayv2_integration.lambda.id}"
}

resource "aws_apigatewayv2_route" "users_crud" {
  for_each  = toset(["GET /users/{id}", "POST /users", "PUT /users/{id}", "DELETE /users/{id}"])
  api_id    = aws_apigatewayv2_api.main.id
  route_key = each.value
  target    = "integrations/${aws_apigatewayv2_integration.lambda.id}"
}

resource "aws_apigatewayv2_stage" "prod" {
  api_id      = aws_apigatewayv2_api.main.id
  name        = var.env
  auto_deploy = true

  access_log_settings {
    destination_arn = aws_cloudwatch_log_group.api_gw.arn
    format = jsonencode({
      requestId = "$context.requestId"
      ip        = "$context.identity.sourceIp"
      latency   = "$context.integrationLatency"
      status    = "$context.status"
      route     = "$context.routeKey"
    })
  }

  default_route_settings {
    throttling_burst_limit = 5000
    throttling_rate_limit  = 10000
  }
}

resource "aws_lambda_permission" "api_gw" {
  action        = "lambda:InvokeFunction"
  function_name = aws_lambda_alias.live.function_name
  qualifier     = aws_lambda_alias.live.name
  principal     = "apigateway.amazonaws.com"
  source_arn    = "${aws_apigatewayv2_api.main.execution_arn}/*/*"
}

output "api_endpoint" {
  value = aws_apigatewayv2_stage.prod.invoke_url
}

GitHub Actions CI/CD

# .github/workflows/deploy.yml
name: Deploy Serverless API
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
  pull_request:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with: { node-version: '20' }
      - run: npm ci && npm test

  deploy:
    needs: test
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
    environment: production
    permissions:
      id-token: write
      contents: read
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v4
        with:
          role-to-assume: arn:aws:iam::123456789:role/github-actions-role
          aws-region: us-east-1

      - name: Setup Terraform
        uses: hashicorp/setup-terraform@v3

      - name: Terraform Apply
        working-directory: infrastructure
        run: |
          terraform init
          terraform apply -auto-approve -var="env=prod"

      - name: Update Lambda Code (fast path)
        run: |
          zip -r lambda.zip src/
          aws lambda update-function-code \
            --function-name myapp-api-prod \
            --zip-file fileb://lambda.zip
          aws lambda wait function-updated \
            --function-name myapp-api-prod
          # Publish new version and update alias
          VERSION=$(aws lambda publish-version \
            --function-name myapp-api-prod \
            --query Version --output text)
          aws lambda update-alias \
            --function-name myapp-api-prod \
            --name live \
            --function-version $VERSION

Project 9: Full DevSecOps Pipeline — Jenkins + SonarQube + Trivy + ArgoCD + Kubernetes

Pipeline Flow
GitHub Push → Jenkins → Unit Tests → SonarQube (SAST) → Docker Build → Trivy (Image Scan)
→ ECR Push → ArgoCD Sync → Kubernetes Deploy → OWASP ZAP (DAST) → Slack Notify

Jenkins Pipeline (Declarative)

// Jenkinsfile
pipeline {
  agent {
    kubernetes {
      yaml """
apiVersion: v1
kind: Pod
spec:
  containers:
  - name: docker
    image: docker:24-dind
    securityContext:
      privileged: true
    volumeMounts:
    - name: docker-sock
      mountPath: /var/run/docker.sock
  - name: tools
    image: amazon/aws-cli:2.x
    command: ['sleep','infinity']
  volumes:
  - name: docker-sock
    hostPath:
      path: /var/run/docker.sock
"""
    }
  }

  environment {
    APP_NAME    = 'myapp'
    ECR_REGISTRY = '123456789.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com'
    GIT_COMMIT_SHORT = sh(script: 'git rev-parse --short HEAD', returnStdout: true).trim()
    IMAGE_TAG   = "${BUILD_NUMBER}-${GIT_COMMIT_SHORT}"
    SONAR_URL   = 'http://sonarqube:9000'
    ARGOCD_SERVER = 'argocd.internal:443'
  }

  options {
    timeout(time: 30, unit: 'MINUTES')
    buildDiscarder(logRotator(numToKeepStr: '20'))
    disableConcurrentBuilds()
  }

  stages {
    stage('Checkout') {
      steps {
        checkout scm
        script { env.GIT_COMMIT_MSG = sh(script: 'git log -1 --pretty=%B', returnStdout: true).trim() }
      }
    }

    stage('Unit Tests') {
      steps {
        container('tools') {
          sh 'npm ci && npm test -- --coverage --ci'
          publishHTML(target: [allowMissing: false, alwaysLinkToLastBuild: true,
            keepAll: true, reportDir: 'coverage', reportFiles: 'index.html',
            reportName: 'Coverage Report'])
        }
      }
      post { always { junit 'test-results/*.xml' } }
    }

    stage('SonarQube Analysis') {
      steps {
        withSonarQubeEnv('SonarQube') {
          sh """
            sonar-scanner \\
              -Dsonar.projectKey=${APP_NAME} \\
              -Dsonar.sources=src \\
              -Dsonar.tests=tests \\
              -Dsonar.javascript.lcov.reportPaths=coverage/lcov.info \\
              -Dsonar.qualitygate.wait=true
          """
        }
      }
    }

    stage('Quality Gate') {
      steps {
        timeout(time: 5, unit: 'MINUTES') {
          waitForQualityGate abortPipeline: true
        }
      }
    }

    stage('Build Docker Image') {
      steps {
        container('docker') {
          sh """
            docker build \\
              --build-arg BUILD_DATE=\$(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ) \\
              --build-arg GIT_COMMIT=${GIT_COMMIT_SHORT} \\
              --label org.opencontainers.image.revision=${GIT_COMMIT_SHORT} \\
              -t ${ECR_REGISTRY}/${APP_NAME}:${IMAGE_TAG} \\
              -t ${ECR_REGISTRY}/${APP_NAME}:latest \\
              .
          """
        }
      }
    }

    stage('Trivy Scan') {
      steps {
        container('tools') {
          sh """
            trivy image \\
              --severity HIGH,CRITICAL \\
              --exit-code 1 \\
              --format table \\
              --ignore-unfixed \\
              --no-progress \\
              ${ECR_REGISTRY}/${APP_NAME}:${IMAGE_TAG}
          """
        }
      }
    }

    stage('Push to ECR') {
      when { branch 'main' }
      steps {
        container('tools') {
          sh """
            aws ecr get-login-password --region us-east-1 | \\
              docker login --username AWS --password-stdin ${ECR_REGISTRY}
            docker push ${ECR_REGISTRY}/${APP_NAME}:${IMAGE_TAG}
            docker push ${ECR_REGISTRY}/${APP_NAME}:latest
          """
        }
      }
    }

    stage('Update GitOps Repo') {
      when { branch 'main' }
      steps {
        withCredentials([sshUserPrivateKey(credentialsId: 'gitops-ssh', keyFileVariable: 'SSH_KEY')]) {
          sh """
            git clone git@github.com:org/gitops-repo.git /tmp/gitops
            cd /tmp/gitops
            # Update image tag in Helm values
            sed -i 's|tag:.*|tag: "${IMAGE_TAG}"|' apps/${APP_NAME}/values-prod.yaml
            git config user.email "jenkins@ci.internal"
            git config user.name "Jenkins"
            git add -A
            git commit -m "ci: update ${APP_NAME} to ${IMAGE_TAG} [skip ci]"
            git push origin main
          """
        }
      }
    }

    stage('ArgoCD Sync') {
      when { branch 'main' }
      steps {
        sh """
          argocd app sync ${APP_NAME} \\
            --server ${ARGOCD_SERVER} \\
            --auth-token \${ARGOCD_TOKEN} \\
            --timeout 300 \\
            --health
        """
      }
    }

    stage('DAST - OWASP ZAP') {
      when { branch 'main' }
      steps {
        sh """
          docker run --rm -v \$(pwd):/zap/wrk/:rw \\
            ghcr.io/zaproxy/zaproxy:stable \\
            zap-api-scan.py \\
            -t https://api.myapp.com/openapi.json \\
            -f openapi \\
            -r zap-report.html \\
            -J zap-report.json \\
            -l WARN
        """
        publishHTML(target: [reportDir: '.', reportFiles: 'zap-report.html',
          reportName: 'ZAP Security Report'])
      }
    }
  }

  post {
    success {
      slackSend(channel: '#deployments', color: 'good',
        message: ":white_check_mark: *${APP_NAME}* `${IMAGE_TAG}` deployed to prod by ${env.GIT_AUTHOR_NAME}")
    }
    failure {
      slackSend(channel: '#deployments', color: 'danger',
        message: ":x: *${APP_NAME}* pipeline failed at stage `${STAGE_NAME}` — <${BUILD_URL}|View Build>")
    }
  }
}

SonarQube + Trivy Docker Compose (Self-hosted)

# docker-compose.yml — DevSecOps tools stack
version: '3.8'
services:
  sonarqube:
    image: sonarqube:community
    environment:
      SONAR_JDBC_URL: jdbc:postgresql://sonar-db:5432/sonar
      SONAR_JDBC_USERNAME: sonar
      SONAR_JDBC_PASSWORD: sonar
    volumes:
      - sonar_data:/opt/sonarqube/data
      - sonar_logs:/opt/sonarqube/logs
    ports: ["9000:9000"]
    ulimits:
      nofile: { soft: 65536, hard: 65536 }
    depends_on: [sonar-db]

  sonar-db:
    image: postgres:15
    environment:
      POSTGRES_USER: sonar
      POSTGRES_PASSWORD: sonar
      POSTGRES_DB: sonar
    volumes: [sonar_db:/var/lib/postgresql/data]

  jenkins:
    image: jenkins/jenkins:lts-jdk17
    privileged: true
    user: root
    volumes:
      - jenkins_home:/var/jenkins_home
      - /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock
    ports: ["8080:8080","50000:50000"]

  nexus:
    image: sonatype/nexus3
    volumes: [nexus_data:/nexus-data]
    ports: ["8081:8081"]

volumes:
  sonar_data: {}
  sonar_logs: {}
  sonar_db: {}
  jenkins_home: {}
  nexus_data: {}
Q: What is "shift-left security" and how does this pipeline implement it?
A: Shift-left means moving security testing earlier in the development lifecycle rather than testing only in production. This pipeline implements it at multiple layers: SonarQube SAST catches vulnerabilities in source code before building; Trivy scans the container image for CVEs before pushing; OWASP ZAP DAST tests the running API; Quality Gates block merges if security score fails. The result: developers get security feedback within minutes of committing code, not weeks after deployment.

Project 10: WordPress HA — EC2 ASG + RDS + EFS + CloudFront + WAF

Architecture
Users → CloudFront (CDN/WAF) → ALB → EC2 ASG (WordPress) → RDS Aurora MySQL (Multi-AZ)
WordPress EC2s share /var/www/html via EFS (shared filesystem)
Secrets Manager (DB password) | ACM (SSL) | Route53 (DNS)

Terraform — WordPress HA Infrastructure

# WordPress HA Terraform

# EFS Filesystem for shared WordPress files
resource "aws_efs_file_system" "wordpress" {
  creation_token   = "wordpress-efs"
  performance_mode = "generalPurpose"
  throughput_mode  = "elastic"
  encrypted        = true

  lifecycle_policy {
    transition_to_ia = "AFTER_30_DAYS"
  }
  tags = { Name = "wordpress-efs" }
}

resource "aws_efs_mount_target" "wordpress" {
  for_each        = toset(module.vpc.private_subnet_ids)
  file_system_id  = aws_efs_file_system.wordpress.id
  subnet_id       = each.value
  security_groups = [aws_security_group.efs.id]
}

resource "aws_efs_access_point" "wordpress" {
  file_system_id = aws_efs_file_system.wordpress.id
  posix_user     = { uid = 33, gid = 33 }    # www-data
  root_directory = {
    path = "/wordpress"
    creation_info = { owner_uid = 33, owner_gid = 33, permissions = "0755" }
  }
}

# RDS Aurora MySQL
resource "aws_rds_cluster" "wordpress" {
  cluster_identifier      = "wordpress-aurora"
  engine                  = "aurora-mysql"
  engine_version          = "8.0.mysql_aurora.3.04.0"
  database_name           = "wordpress"
  master_username         = "wpadmin"
  manage_master_user_password = true    # Secrets Manager rotation
  db_subnet_group_name    = aws_db_subnet_group.main.name
  vpc_security_group_ids  = [aws_security_group.rds.id]
  backup_retention_period = 7
  preferred_backup_window = "03:00-04:00"
  skip_final_snapshot     = false
  final_snapshot_identifier = "wordpress-final-${formatdate("YYYYMMDDhhmmss", timestamp())}"
  enabled_cloudwatch_logs_exports = ["audit","error","general","slowquery"]
  deletion_protection     = true
  tags = local.common_tags
}

resource "aws_rds_cluster_instance" "wordpress" {
  count              = 2
  cluster_identifier = aws_rds_cluster.wordpress.id
  instance_class     = "db.r6g.large"
  engine             = aws_rds_cluster.wordpress.engine
  publicly_accessible = false
}

# Launch Template with user data
resource "aws_launch_template" "wordpress" {
  name_prefix   = "wordpress-"
  image_id      = data.aws_ami.amazon_linux.id
  instance_type = "t3.medium"
  key_name      = var.key_name

  iam_instance_profile { name = aws_iam_instance_profile.wordpress.name }
  vpc_security_group_ids = [aws_security_group.wordpress.id]

  user_data = base64encode(templatefile("${path.module}/userdata.sh.tpl", {
    efs_id       = aws_efs_file_system.wordpress.id
    efs_ap_id    = aws_efs_access_point.wordpress.id
    db_host      = aws_rds_cluster.wordpress.endpoint
    db_secret    = aws_rds_cluster.wordpress.master_user_secret[0].secret_arn
    wp_domain    = var.domain_name
    region       = var.aws_region
  }))

  block_device_mappings {
    device_name = "/dev/xvda"
    ebs {
      volume_size           = 20
      volume_type           = "gp3"
      encrypted             = true
      delete_on_termination = true
    }
  }

  metadata_options {
    http_endpoint               = "enabled"
    http_tokens                 = "required"    # IMDSv2
    http_put_response_hop_limit = 1
  }

  tag_specifications {
    resource_type = "instance"
    tags = merge(local.common_tags, { Name = "wordpress-web" })
  }
}

# ASG
resource "aws_autoscaling_group" "wordpress" {
  name                = "wordpress-asg"
  vpc_zone_identifier = module.vpc.private_subnet_ids
  target_group_arns   = [aws_lb_target_group.wordpress.arn]
  min_size            = 2
  max_size            = 10
  desired_capacity    = 2
  health_check_type         = "ELB"
  health_check_grace_period = 300

  launch_template {
    id      = aws_launch_template.wordpress.id
    version = "$Latest"
  }

  instance_refresh {
    strategy = "Rolling"
    preferences {
      min_healthy_percentage = 50
      instance_warmup        = 300
    }
  }
}

# CloudFront with WAF
resource "aws_cloudfront_distribution" "wordpress" {
  origin {
    domain_name = aws_lb.wordpress.dns_name
    origin_id   = "ALB"
    custom_origin_config {
      http_port              = 80
      https_port             = 443
      origin_protocol_policy = "https-only"
      origin_ssl_protocols   = ["TLSv1.2"]
    }
    custom_header {
      name  = "X-Origin-Secret"
      value = random_password.origin_secret.result
    }
  }

  enabled             = true
  aliases             = [var.domain_name, "www.${var.domain_name}"]
  default_root_object = "index.php"

  default_cache_behavior {
    allowed_methods        = ["DELETE","GET","HEAD","OPTIONS","PATCH","POST","PUT"]
    cached_methods         = ["GET","HEAD"]
    target_origin_id       = "ALB"
    viewer_protocol_policy = "redirect-to-https"
    compress               = true

    forwarded_values {
      query_string = true
      cookies { forward = "whitelist"; whitelisted_names = ["wordpress_*","wp_*","comment_*"] }
      headers = ["Host","Authorization","CloudFront-Forwarded-Proto"]
    }

    cache_policy_id = aws_cloudfront_cache_policy.wp_dynamic.id
  }

  # Cache static assets aggressively
  ordered_cache_behavior {
    path_pattern     = "/wp-content/*"
    allowed_methods  = ["GET","HEAD"]
    cached_methods   = ["GET","HEAD"]
    target_origin_id = "ALB"
    viewer_protocol_policy = "redirect-to-https"
    compress = true
    default_ttl = 86400
    max_ttl     = 604800
    forwarded_values {
      query_string = false
      cookies { forward = "none" }
    }
  }

  web_acl_id = aws_wafv2_web_acl.wordpress.arn

  viewer_certificate {
    acm_certificate_arn      = aws_acm_certificate.wordpress.arn
    ssl_support_method       = "sni-only"
    minimum_protocol_version = "TLSv1.2_2021"
  }

  restrictions {
    geo_restriction { restriction_type = "none" }
  }
}

WordPress User Data Script

#!/bin/bash
# userdata.sh.tpl — WordPress setup on EC2
set -euo pipefail

# Install packages
dnf update -y
dnf install -y amazon-efs-utils php8.2 php8.2-{fpm,mysqlnd,gd,xml,mbstring,opcache,redis,zip} nginx

# Mount EFS
mkdir -p /var/www/html
echo "${efs_id}:/ /var/www/html efs _netdev,tls,accesspoint=${efs_ap_id} 0 0" >> /etc/fstab
mount -a

# Get DB credentials from Secrets Manager
DB_SECRET=$(aws secretsmanager get-secret-value \
  --secret-id "${db_secret}" --region "${region}" \
  --query SecretString --output text)
DB_PASSWORD=$(echo $DB_SECRET | python3 -c "import sys,json; print(json.load(sys.stdin)['password'])")

# Install WordPress (only if not already done — EFS shared)
if [ ! -f /var/www/html/wp-config.php ]; then
  cd /tmp
  curl -O https://wordpress.org/latest.tar.gz
  tar -xzf latest.tar.gz
  cp -r wordpress/. /var/www/html/
  chown -R www-data:www-data /var/www/html

  # Configure wp-config.php
  cp /var/www/html/wp-config-sample.php /var/www/html/wp-config.php
  sed -i "s/database_name_here/wordpress/" /var/www/html/wp-config.php
  sed -i "s/username_here/wpadmin/" /var/www/html/wp-config.php
  sed -i "s/password_here/$DB_PASSWORD/" /var/www/html/wp-config.php
  sed -i "s/localhost/${db_host}/" /var/www/html/wp-config.php

  # Add Redis object cache config
  cat >> /var/www/html/wp-config.php << 'EOF'
define('WP_REDIS_HOST', 'redis.internal');
define('WP_REDIS_PORT', 6379);
define('WP_CACHE', true);
EOF
fi

# Configure PHP-FPM
sed -i 's/user = apache/user = nginx/' /etc/php-fpm.d/www.conf
sed -i 's/group = apache/group = nginx/' /etc/php-fpm.d/www.conf

# Start services
systemctl enable --now nginx php-fpm
systemctl enable --now amazon-ssm-agent

Reusable ECS Service Module

# modules/ecs-service/main.tf
variable "service_name"    { type = string }
variable "cluster_id"      { type = string }
variable "container_image" { type = string }
variable "container_port"  { type = number }
variable "cpu"             { type = number; default = 256 }
variable "memory"          { type = number; default = 512 }
variable "desired_count"   { type = number; default = 2 }
variable "target_group_arn" { type = string }
variable "subnets"         { type = list(string) }
variable "security_groups" { type = list(string) }
variable "environment_vars" { type = list(object({ name=string, value=string })) }
variable "secrets"         { type = list(object({ name=string, valueFrom=string })) }
variable "task_role_arn"   { type = string }

resource "aws_ecs_task_definition" "this" {
  family                   = var.service_name
  network_mode             = "awsvpc"
  requires_compatibilities = ["FARGATE"]
  cpu                      = var.cpu
  memory                   = var.memory
  execution_role_arn       = aws_iam_role.execution.arn
  task_role_arn            = var.task_role_arn

  container_definitions = jsonencode([{
    name  = var.service_name
    image = var.container_image
    portMappings = [{
      name          = var.service_name
      containerPort = var.container_port
      protocol      = "tcp"
      appProtocol   = "http"
    }]
    environment = var.environment_vars
    secrets     = var.secrets
    logConfiguration = {
      logDriver = "awslogs"
      options = {
        awslogs-group         = "/ecs/${var.service_name}"
        awslogs-region        = data.aws_region.current.name
        awslogs-stream-prefix = "ecs"
      }
    }
    healthCheck = {
      command     = ["CMD-SHELL", "curl -f http://localhost:${var.container_port}/health || exit 1"]
      interval    = 30
      timeout     = 5
      retries     = 3
      startPeriod = 60
    }
  }])
}

resource "aws_ecs_service" "this" {
  name            = var.service_name
  cluster         = var.cluster_id
  task_definition = aws_ecs_task_definition.this.arn
  desired_count   = var.desired_count
  launch_type     = "FARGATE"

  network_configuration {
    subnets         = var.subnets
    security_groups = var.security_groups
    assign_public_ip = false
  }

  load_balancer {
    target_group_arn = var.target_group_arn
    container_name   = var.service_name
    container_port   = var.container_port
  }

  service_connect_configuration {
    enabled   = true
    namespace = aws_service_discovery_private_dns_namespace.main.arn
    service {
      port_name = var.service_name
      client_alias {
        port     = var.container_port
        dns_name = var.service_name
      }
    }
  }

  deployment_circuit_breaker {
    enable   = true
    rollback = true
  }

  deployment_controller { type = "ECS" }

  lifecycle {
    ignore_changes = [task_definition, desired_count]
  }
}

# Auto Scaling
resource "aws_appautoscaling_target" "this" {
  max_capacity       = 10
  min_capacity       = var.desired_count
  resource_id        = "service/${var.cluster_id}/${var.service_name}"
  scalable_dimension = "ecs:service:DesiredCount"
  service_namespace  = "ecs"
}

resource "aws_appautoscaling_policy" "cpu" {
  name               = "${var.service_name}-cpu-scaling"
  policy_type        = "TargetTrackingScaling"
  resource_id        = aws_appautoscaling_target.this.resource_id
  scalable_dimension = aws_appautoscaling_target.this.scalable_dimension
  service_namespace  = aws_appautoscaling_target.this.service_namespace

  target_tracking_scaling_policy_configuration {
    predefined_metric_specification { predefined_metric_type = "ECSServiceAverageCPUUtilization" }
    target_value       = 60.0
    scale_in_cooldown  = 300
    scale_out_cooldown = 60
  }
}

# environments/prod/main.tf — Compose all services
module "auth_service" {
  source         = "../../modules/ecs-service"
  service_name   = "auth-service"
  cluster_id     = module.ecs_cluster.id
  container_image = "${module.ecr["auth"].url}:${var.auth_tag}"
  container_port = 3001
  cpu    = 512
  memory = 1024
  target_group_arn = module.alb.target_groups["auth"].arn
  subnets          = module.vpc.private_subnets
  security_groups  = [aws_security_group.ecs_tasks.id]
  task_role_arn    = module.iam_task_role["auth"].arn
  environment_vars = [
    { name = "JWT_SECRET_ARN", value = aws_secretsmanager_secret.jwt.arn },
    { name = "REDIS_HOST",     value = module.elasticache.endpoint }
  ]
  secrets = [
    { name = "JWT_SECRET", valueFrom = aws_secretsmanager_secret.jwt.arn }
  ]
}

Multi-Service GitHub Actions

# .github/workflows/deploy-service.yml
name: Deploy Microservice
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
    paths:
      - 'services/**'
      - '.github/workflows/deploy-service.yml'

jobs:
  detect-changes:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    outputs:
      services: ${{ steps.detect.outputs.services }}
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
        with: { fetch-depth: 2 }
      - id: detect
        run: |
          CHANGED=$(git diff --name-only HEAD~1 HEAD | grep '^services/' | cut -d/ -f2 | sort -u | jq -R -s -c 'split("\n")[:-1]')
          echo "services=$CHANGED" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT

  deploy:
    needs: detect-changes
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    if: needs.detect-changes.outputs.services != '[]'
    strategy:
      matrix:
        service: ${{ fromJSON(needs.detect-changes.outputs.services) }}
    permissions:
      id-token: write
      contents: read
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v4
        with:
          role-to-assume: ${{ secrets.AWS_DEPLOY_ROLE }}
          aws-region: us-east-1

      - name: Login to ECR
        id: login-ecr
        uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecr-login@v2

      - name: Build and Push
        env:
          ECR_REGISTRY: ${{ steps.login-ecr.outputs.registry }}
          IMAGE_TAG: ${{ github.sha }}
        run: |
          cd services/${{ matrix.service }}
          docker build -t $ECR_REGISTRY/${{ matrix.service }}:$IMAGE_TAG .
          docker push $ECR_REGISTRY/${{ matrix.service }}:$IMAGE_TAG

      - name: Deploy to ECS
        run: |
          # Force new deployment — picks up latest image if using :sha tag
          aws ecs update-service \
            --cluster prod-cluster \
            --service ${{ matrix.service }} \
            --force-new-deployment \
            --region us-east-1

          # Wait for stability
          aws ecs wait services-stable \
            --cluster prod-cluster \
            --services ${{ matrix.service }}
